Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old days "contused cure," and is that you do at the back of the patient who has this disease the hairs that he have or front, then make III cuts or front equally according to the length of the front; and let one of the cuts be as II should all remove the front downhill down until the nape, and the other II as II ribs above the papers, and keep away from the incision of the arteries which are as II ribs above the papers; and move your hand from the continuation of the II jaws, and let each wound the quantity of III does across joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of drapes his for wiping the blood, then put the spatula acute of II parts of this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	of the incision which is from behind the temple until the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the two incisions to all the skin that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula fully.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if it is put in the first cut the instrument which is called "cultellaire," and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting towards the flesh near the heart, and the rib groove towards the bone, and the point as long as it comes to the middle furrow. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens the heart, and then another part make in the middle fissure until the other end; and then extract blood evenly, and express the place for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and asile, and guard that no abscess comes there; and at the third day untie the thread, and there administer great planty of lukewarm water, then the cure of basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures which one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When any come with acute catarrh, and you see the eyes watery and small, and the vision weakened, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where they are parted a sharp pain occurs, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh do not come from many veins, and the cure that there is, such is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to pull back his forehead, then make a large incision between the eyebrows, and another along the ridge above the eye socket. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it begins with the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the meal; and when the bone is discovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then carefully between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton, and linen bandages; then tie above cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until cartilage begins to form, then cure it with drying things, that make cartilage grow.   
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of flower of wheat and 4 parts of colophony, and make a plaster from them; and administer it in these wounds to prevent cartilage growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which goes into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or stone of mine or something similar as iron; or seeds, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing thing such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then set the ear in the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and let him sneeze with a condition, and plug his nostrils when sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and raise the ear upwards.  
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes force by this cure; and if it does not come force, to him is administered the extraction with subtle pincers, for this is the form. 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a subtle oncine of small doubleure; and if it does not come out by that, make a snare of wire and insert the head of the snare or opening into the ear forcefully, and plug what is around the snare with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter there with the snare; then pull the thing out forcefully, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take some gut which they use to catch birds, and put on a small instrument which is suitable for doing this, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the gut upon the stone or whatever thing it is, and pull out forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not emerge from all these things that we have said, then you hasten to cut the ear as an abscess comes forth, and spasms; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient healthy in the head, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be as a moon, as far as you come to the stone, then the bone according to your power, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot issue forth, then administer i. spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer incision to that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with subtle pincers and with suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water therefore that falls into the ear it is necessary for the patient to use externally of condiments first, and fill the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it has been cured by this, it is good.  
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not work this way, take many stones according to the length of your finger, thin and light, and heat them a little in fire; and put one in the patient’s ear, and let it rise up from his foot on the other side, and hold another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease to make this of stones until the water is completely out, and so it will all be gone; and if you see that it does not work, take a straw, and put one end in the ear, and the other end in the fire until the top of the straw burns; then redo another part with other straws until the water is all out, as we have said about the stone.  
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large body which one can feel, then administer extraction with tweezers; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the cure does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if there appears no worms, then you treat them with subtle tweezers, and if they do not appear, then take the canine of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.  
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck them out all the way around; do this often until all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to issue, so stuff the cotton in the ear as I said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, so administer distillations that the ancients have proved in the excision of worms, and you will find them or treating of distillations; and if distill your oils and your medicines in the ear to all this instrument, of which is the form as you see:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be of silver or copper, narrow below to one small holes, and above open for distilling; and for pressing inside the distillation one instrument of copper well made for that, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the tip conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and what you want of your medicines in the chain, and the chain be in the ear; then put inside the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finished at the end of the ear; and feel the patient inside, and let the distillations be one pock heated at the fire then when it is distilled in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by wound closure, or by flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes in the ear if one cannot see it; and sometimes it happens that there is i.e., a little piece of fur in the ear, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes in inside if one cannot see it, is of great healing in more dispositions, and in this one sees that you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening apparent, then the work has all these spatumile from which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be aged and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or core of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, as long as that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ear opening is pierced with a tool, take a fine and light razor and heat it on fire, then place it in the ear canal.  
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opening where the patient feels pain upon hearing it, pierce lightly, and guard that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the breadth of the hole, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on ground vitriol; and if you see swollen the ear, then it is necessary that you withdraw the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are or treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the sheet of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This treatment that comes on sheets of paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry, so it is necessary to spread them with forceps and tweezers, and scrape off a spatula from their roots; then put on top of them ground vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it there is no decor, then cauterize it with a subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterization after the incision will be cured; and many times they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times in papers come to the eyes things that seem gravel in its form and in its hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hailstorm", and it is a gathering of moisture large in the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the hailstone moves on one side and the other, and it is a light thing to know; then make the hole wide, then peel each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and the cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a little of the paper, do not grieve the patient; and if the fissure is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the flesh restores it soon and hinders char. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the inside of the ear towards the upper part, so turn the paper, and being the hail to tweezers, and cut and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does not grieve anything; and when the hail is cut, leave the eye with salty water, and cure the place of that which injures flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is created in the webs of the papers above, and this happens more to children than adults, and grieves them greatly at their eyes, and they get the cataracts in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces down, and sleep on top, and are their papers under their eyebrows moist that the inflammation and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye. 
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your thumbs and feel the exhumer between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head on your thigh; and then take one drape of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach of each part, then put it on top; and press with your fingers on both sides, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture at the spatula sharp a fissure of the wide, and be not more great than the wound one makes at the vein; and make the leather in depth as much as you come to the exirnach; and in many dispositions comes exirnach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove then with one piece of linen cloth between your fingers at the outside, and turn your hand right and left as much as it is spread; and guard that you do not add in the fissure, that you do not come to all the spatula until the eye, that you do not bleach it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, then carefully widen the split until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in warm and cold water, and place on top, and bandage firmly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind herbs and put them on to corrupt the moisture that is lingering. 
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure as long as he is healed. 
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, so its care is with plasters soothing until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born arranged other than the natural ones, and they are aged, they harm the eyes and bring many kinds of diseases like tears accustomed and softening of the papers and albuginea, as much as this is cause of destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery together fire, or by medicine ague according to that it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and suture or by canes, according to that I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient on your own, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then there is brought a needle to .i. thread above; and let this be below the edge of the paper or where the hair grows near these hairs, and carry .i. thread upward to all the paper, and turn it back to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, under the hairs arranged, at all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then rule on top of the paper a figure of an arch, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see lift the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs it, one should cut a large quantity of the paper according to what the paper is soft; then make along the whole spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the top with a large tear down to small; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the ointment into one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it all off; then assemble the two lips with a stitch of a needle on all the fine wool thread, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of the hairs on the two eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take no care of it, then leave the stitch and the threads up to three days or four; then cure the wound without stitching with dry and constricting things, because the paper revives at the bottom of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitch is moved (as the ancients say), and this work without fear; and if in another way: and that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have shown, to three incisions detached according to the form which is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut that which ascends with small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you don't have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing isn't equal, take a needle where it has the thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put the other thread along the big tear, and the second thread along the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then raise your hand equally, and raise all the skin on what you have marked, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it befits that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make 2 canes by art, and 2 subtle liens as long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and cut the two heads of 2 parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the 2 canes of the 2 parts formed; and let it stay like this for several days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and carry, as long as it dries by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, if the cut has some force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn shut, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the II canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:  
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you prick a fine needle, and put through it one thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk neatly, and tie the heads of the threads; then place the patient's head on your healthy; and be so that the work is clear because it is a subtle and fine work, then put the needle into all the chase at the root of the hair adjusted, and make it pierce the paper carefully until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out from all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair sets in its place and the flesh grows on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of the natural hooves, and raise it with that one or where you leave it, as long as it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness which is called "alacratitis" or the rot comes in the eye, if there are two manners: one natural, and the other unnatural. 
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden force of wound or incision or cautery, and similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work on it is that you split that joint, and loosen its lips, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not proper that you use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but there is work of softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rosehip or elm and flaxseed be cooked, and the diachylon ointment melted in any oil, and wrap a tent, and cure with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close again according to the form it was before; and these operations that we have said are only addresses for this illness so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This sickness that is dislocat is truly called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you prick an awl, which has double thread, and place it in the skin, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the threads come into the two shoulders of the skin; then the skin is above the entire awl, and the cut comes with a spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what it should, it is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the split, and turn the paper, and make two slits where it costs inside the paper; and let the heads of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove the flesh according to the quantity that its cost is raised below, from what follows the paper, then adjust the two severed parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then care for it as we have said with softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a tear or stitching or cautery, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papers, and according to what has been said before; then place between the .ij. leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip anything of all their power how they make it return the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary of work and instruments in more dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper carefully
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering happens to the hand of a man in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor perform its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the extent as the pinches, until you cut what is adhered to the spatula subtle, which is not too sharp nor too trenchant, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula too sharp or they would pierce the eye; and be your incision, by which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it heals all that assembly, and sometimes in the eye salt water, and the rise of fresh water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in an abundance of egg; and after the third day use the collyrium and the things again as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in two manners: one is like .ij. hard, and one other which is not nervous, but is like white frozen moisture, and when you touch it with iron and you cauterize it with pincers, it cannot be moved; and one and the other semblance begins toward the large tear duct, and crosses poc and poc until it covers the entire view and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens his eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coils the angle with small pliers, and the essence above; then take a needle, and put on it .i. hair of horse, or cowhide, or ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the tip of the needle a poc and insert it into the angle, and pierce it through the entire needle, and tie the angle with a thread and lift it above, and strip all the hair along the side of the angle which follows the root and silk to the hair up to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear duct with all the small spatula and as little force as possible, and leave the natural char or tear duct, so that through the incision the body of tears does not come customarily; and at any time extend the angle solely on the needle, and thread, as we have said; then strip it all over the small spatula from this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of wool crushed, and with the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as much as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not yet nerved, and you cannot push the needle, and the awl cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, operate on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light bit sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail upwards subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason is quickened, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of litharge and red ointment and crushed wool, and stop the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same work, as long as it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess, then cauterize it and cure the abscess first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh from the tear harms the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the incision and cut a part and not half so that no tear fluid comes; then instill into the eye a red colic which is made of lead white.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red flesh, and covers the eyelid and restrained upon the papers and turns to the fire, and seems like a rose from a balcony; and the work is that the patient puts his head in your healthy, then the works the eyes, and coil all that flesh as needles suitable to them, and sustains it with force; then cut the first flesh, and go all cutting to the razor until the end, and take care that you do not injure the eye during the work; and be the incision of the spatula as we have said in the incision of the angle and small forces of which one removes the white, as the form after this chapter shows; and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silk ground or you distill red wine and similar corrosive medicines, and put on top of the fire cotton with an egg white, so that it be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the without wool covers you, and you doubt a hot abscess, so leave the eye and cure the abscess with things soothing a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make as long as flesh is adjusted in the eye by this semblance.  
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it behooves you to apply the cure of each weak oil of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Veins are red that are covered over the eye, and they take away from their sight and weaken the eye every day. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary for the first that you look at if the eye, whether it is whole, or not, and there is no other disease except for the eyeball; therefore, the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your chest, then suspend those veins all the way up according to his wisdom, and let the bandages be subtle double according to this form. 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let two lines be by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see removing those veins out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and do this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut other than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye collyrium green and red to corrupt what is remaining of the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is calmed and is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and medicine burning hot according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut on the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instruments of what here is the form; and it is called "sharp head," and it is made of iron for one head reont, and it is pointed like a file as much as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two, and press your hand a little so much as you know that that corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the opening is soldered, and flesh is born, and the bow of the body is soldered, and it remains like this for 40 days, and it does not renew and is not suppurating, know that it is healed; if no, there is nothing else but to bring back the fistula to its opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered take the forest according to this form, and let the head of iron be at 3 angles, and the shaft be tapered until the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and keep your hand away from the eye's point, then turn to the whole forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he holds his hand on his nose; and then return the place of dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh is born and hardens its parts, then the matter goes to the nose; thus it is a lighter thing for the patient.  
de l’issue de l’oil	from the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open entirely throughout, and there is no discharge to the knee, nor diminution, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then cleanse, then put him on suction cups or a heater without hurting so that it sucks; then place on the eye one sheet made of cotton wool and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one by four, and then place one upon the other according to the quantity that the eye has need for; then strain it from above with a hard bandage form, and recommence the suction cups so that they suck without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the sheets soften, then it is necessary that you strain it very much; then remove the sheet after the day and the night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not; then recommence the plastering and the cloths and the sheet and the suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the dislocation of cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the woven cloth, then open it, and it comes forth full of papers like grains of resin, and it is expectable to see; therefore if you want to cover it, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the lamier part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie a part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put the other half-eyed oil in abundance of yolk; and let it stay until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape on each side of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes then give great appearance, pierce them with a subtle spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and bring down the eyes, and put them in immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is nothing else but a bulge that is assembled in the eye, appearing like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it until you see the bulge come up to your eyes; then be ens fichie, and do not descend and let be discomposed the light, and let the patient see things as he would; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bulge is not arranged as we have said. 
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and scrape over the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and crown, until it is issued; and when it is out, drop into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the arrows of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the resemblances of the swords in the division, and those that it befits to perceive; so in working according to health.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the sun, and tie his good eye and hold it firmly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left, or in your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument that is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the width of a hair in the whiteness of the eye at the part of the lesser tear, then push the instrument that is called "almagda" virtuously, and restore your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black; and this is the crown of the eye; if you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument until where the liquid is, then express it down one way after another. 
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water descends now, if the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water rises back up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and it does not rise, gently withdraw the almagda by turning your hand poc and poc; and then put back into water a poc of silk gemma, and leave from this the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by way of cover an oiled felt or softened linen, in rose oil and a little white of egg, and tie with the sound eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top like a commin with abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it behooves that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit," for this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too far in byforce, but make it subtle, then put almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, equip the patient the sleeper coming, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be deprived of all movements, and take light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you apply this, for those who ascend quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, that you unlock the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who appease the abscess; and when it is calmed, then unbind the view and put on its face the orilliet to cover any day, and be thus in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he goes out of the house here and there, and converts himself in his case; and knows that none of disciples must interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almond paste pierced, so that one sucks the liquid, but all the same I never saw any in our land, nor did I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almond, because those who do not know them see them; and be of rain properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of each of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the birth
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At no time are born or found joined together chars diverse, of which there are some that seem scorpions at the foot of the legs; and if there are such ones where it has char inflamed with dark color, and if there is char flesh of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these chariots which is inflamed and not yet split, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils and place the oncine to those chariots, and the trais outwards; then cut what you can sustain with the sharp subtle spatula from one side, until you know that this chariot is completely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains which one cannot cover, then open it completely i.e. with instruments subtle light; so that nothing remains; and if without tear or abscess, cauterize it as is proper; and if it are malignant abscesses, then haste and cauterize them until the blood be extinguished and all the pus is removed, then pour on vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut: therefore it is necessary that you put I linen thread a little thick, and be knotted by the hands of us, and have between each knot a space of I must or less; and put the patient's shoulder of the thread in his nose to its power, and pull until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many times do children like this at school, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel them one after the other in being as we who are or thread.  
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do as much as you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it straight back into place as before; do this for III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the wound a poultice of lead for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, for which one distills the oils and medicines onto the wound:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or iron, resembling a lamp open, as a band, and conduct it thus also; and if you see, then make a closed band, and let the instruments be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
