Many times a disease is born at the bone of birth called "telul," and it grows and becomes great after, until it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and push out all the bone, then put upon its place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, one should beware if it is hard, of bad color, of poor feeling: one should not touch it with iron for it is an incured abscess, for when one cuts it any time, there comes great evil to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of bad color, and you see that one can cut all of it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry things and restraining.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these workbook cartilages, it profits little, for in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then adjust the two lips together with a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, then it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and restrain them, and powder over powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and put on the powders a piece of ointment of strong or another mending ointment, and let it stay until it falls off by itself, then treat it with oil until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's mouths there come within the lips abscesses hard, seeming to grains of seeds, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut above each one, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then put in the place after the incision of vitriol ground, until the blood be stanched; and then the leave of ease, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	from the root of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is born on the gums flesh knotted, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the blood run; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other powders restraining and drying; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellow and green as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is putrid; so you should make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do of blackness and greenish hue, and jaundice and other spots, until they are wiped out; and if one removes what there is at the first attempt, it is good; if those do not, he recommences on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments for removing, according to what the work shows, because the scraper with which one removes outside the teeth has other forms than that with which one removes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait for the drawing as much as you can, because one should not do otherwise; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure pain, it is necessary that you are certain of which tooth aches. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain of the sick person leaves and thinks that it is a tooth of Saint, and makes milk the good tooth; and altogether does not depart the pain by this, as long as the evil remains, because we have already wanted to do this with our saints; and when you are well certain about the tooth hurting, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth to all i. spatula strong to ward off the gums from all parts; then move it to your two or tongs subtly at the first point and point, until it is well removed, then firmly affirm the tongs; and let the patient's head in your saint between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move. 
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth straightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and put it inside each side gently, and move it as you did first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it is necessary that you fill it with bandages, where the holes are; and if you restrain it gently with tweezers so that it does not break when restrained; and it is necessary to work very skillfully around the gum to dislodge the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient through the malice of the root greater pains than the first.  
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant physicians who by their haste and boldness sometimes break a bone and bring no remedy for what we have recounted; but they cause to come often through this incision great illness for the roots that remain there, or for the broken bone, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, apply the place with vitriol ground; and if that does not work, cauterize it.  
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, as to how one pulls out the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and be toothed for to grip firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the teat, it is necessary that you put upon it cotton moistened with butter for a day or two. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eye is closed, put in the tongs that are called "algefri," so that the head seems like a bird's beak; and make them inside like a file, and this is the shape.  
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say a spatula, because of this its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with those, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are in front in the arrangement of teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pliers, of which here is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it cannot break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not all counted; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the illness show them, for there are such maladies where the old ones do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, or he can, then seek the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help with gestures, from this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can hold it and remove it; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in virgins, it behooves that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file it nor trim it; therefore the ray; and if it is pierced with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and resembles a little beak, and be of sharpened iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope little by little in hands days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, then the file of a certain form like this is.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in hands days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plain at the end to all none razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness so that it be equal, so that it does not bleed the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front breaks, or by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it to make it move without it coming out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and it is no use; if they are required to be restrained with a thread of gold, because the silver thread becomes green and rotten, but gold never changes; and let the thread be medium neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see it necessary to advance the teeth, then take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the broken pieces between the good teeth, if there are one or more, until you come sagely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and sagely, so that it does not move at all; and let your tie be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grip the chies of the wire with pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth and the one that is broken, and set it so that it does not touch the tongue; then leave it tight as much as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the wires break, then restrain it with another wire; let it remain and serve like this throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, fresh against fresh, as we have said; and no one should intervene unless they are wise and experienced, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from a piece of bone, and it is placed in the space where there is a deficiency, and it is restrained as we have said, and it remains and serves this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to close the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this bond comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a stitched wound; and the work is such that you operate the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous tie large, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from the welding of a wound, then put the awl and cut the large ligament; and guard that the cutting be not too deep, for the artery which is beneath; and when you have done, lift the place with rose water and oil, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and apply this to the patient every night, that the places may not weld together. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put on the place powdered vitriol; and if the blood does not stop, then cauterize it with the fine cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatment until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rotten color or black or hard, so that the sick person does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then put in the probe, and make it with a spatula subtle, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the blood does not stop at your work, then put on top powdered vitriol until it is scorched, then return to your work as long as you draw out all matter; then lift the location of oil and water, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come from within the throat boils that are called «godath», and these they call properly the II almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, if you take care: if it is abscesses hard of small sense and of fusse color, then do not touch them with iron.  
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid bloodletting; but let it be left until it is ripe, and then you will cut it open, or it would break on its own; and if it is of white color, and the root is thin, have your instrument ready to cover, but first look if the abscess heals and is calmed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his shoulders be in your health, and he opens his mouth and the surgeon puts the instrument between his hands, and presses the tongue below with all the instrument, of this is the form; and be it of silver or steel as fine as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the oncine and stick it in the almond, and pull it upward as much as you can; and do nothing with the fabrics with it, then cut with the instrument, from which this is the form, that seems like a force; and anyway, the chief are curved, and one place the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument present, then cut it with pliers, from which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be sharp on one side, and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold and thus, and if there is evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranate fruits be cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them then like the two almonds accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was near inside her throat, that is to say the small abscess; and I had closed up the whole throat well, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained thus for one day or two. 
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high it had to be put two fingers through each of the two openings. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I placed therefore so much and put it in one incision, then I pulled the thread outwards, and in pulling a large portion of bowel; then I refit another part into the other place of the two, and worked the mouth and pressed the tongue; after I put the needle into these abscesses, and copied a part, and there came out only a bit of blood; and thus was opened the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I tightened it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I parted from these parts, and know only that God did to her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the shape of the grape becomes raised at the base and it is plump and long, it is called “perpendicular”; and if it is less thick and rounded, it is called “grape”. 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the pus of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of blood color or black, then it is necessary that you drain the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril to the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument of which we have made mention before; then place the needle in the eye, and pull it out, and cut with the II instruments that I have said in the incision of the II almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice, and to speech; and after the incision, use those things that we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of being cut, then it is necessary that you use something to the cauterization of the senses of fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute.  
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy one, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with a sharp quick shoe, so that it is not too thick nor too light; and in employing the end of this instrument, for this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And has or chief a hair where one puts the medicine, as the handle of a spoon, and puts the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient lies on his side, so that the saliva and the mucus come from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the breast; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it being nursed and the stings of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the vein above, as long as the cotton dries on the grape; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it dry, and wait after .iiij. days or .v.. And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton wrapped in butter, and purify what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured by gargarismes until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble them all or any of them in one pot, and put them therein, and boil; and the pot should be well glued with firm earth, and inside the pot has one instrument shaped according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it silver or bronze, and be one of the shoulders thrust into the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the grape by the vein, until the grape is mortified; afterward he starts over, as long as the grape dries up, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a dog and put inside its head a piece of wood, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the piece of wood does not make the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is good cure altogether health. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens to the throat bone or spine of fish, or anything else; so therefore it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing; and those that do not appear to you and are returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it will throw out the thing dry through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one mouthful of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to its place, it will be felt, and then you will draw out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take one instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head high lifted; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come to it, nor thrust in the bone; and it is better that the patient thrusts the instrument, because he shall know if the thing is hoarse; if then he thrusts down, or he draws it forth equally throughout the instrument, as long as it is forth.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat cutting
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is given to the patient without bloodletting, as I have said in the division; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all the little pincers or subtle forceps that are suitable for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that doesn't work, take a sheared dog hair and put it in the throat of the sick person, then put where the end of the dog hair is hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And he keeps the patient in water all day. 
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the cup of cold water, and work the mouth, and place it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he falls.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not heal as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the smoking of grapes; do this many times, because it will heal without suffering. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot or it has charcoal in it, and let the bottom be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in this put the head of the instrument; then you throw your fumigation in it, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not go out, but comes up to the sinus; and the sinus will now fall, and if it doesn't fall, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and chew things salty and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary that it be done by this governance.  
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the sinus is, when one can see it, like tongs curved to enter into the throat; and it has the semblance of a bird's beak, and there is roughness from lime so that what it takes, it cannot leave; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similarities of abscesses are, according to what the memory comes after this in one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in II manners which one is in its same appearance, and from that which holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess of the head are other than those of the foundation, and the abscess of the flesh is other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if on abscesses one must not pierce until the bowel is mature according to its fulfillment; and if on such ones that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, as abscesses which are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left until it is completely rotten, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, therefore this is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal limb. When it is near the foundation, then pierce it so that it matures. 
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the piercing of the abscess which is mature according to its accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the fever departs, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where most dependent the location of the abscess, and where it opens more; and whether the piercing is long in the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equal where there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these which are dislocated, according to the member. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is well that you let the opening remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.  
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before those things, then the body of the vein will be lengthened from him, and it is full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the members need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring to small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the heart, and to cover; when it is become as I drapes, and is softened, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils: and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such which one covers as the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses of the angles; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and seeming cuts. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, like a superficial abscess, it behooves you to pierce it plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain a part; then plug the abscess until the other day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times from great to small, until the pus is gone entirely; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit often trembles with the issue of the bowels, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not despair. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, then wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat cut, then administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that it comes against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then the bone, and cure with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bloodletting happens in your work, then administer cold water and apply it, and wet the drapery, and place it on the bleeding spot many times.  
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the discharge of blood persists, administer governance and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is wintertime, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is summertime, and the wound is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on damp cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then undo the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it behoves to know universally in cures of abscesses: Or I have said how one must go before the cures of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	Of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the heart of the head comes small abscesses, and are manners of us that are in fabrics, as well as the joint of a gooseberry, and much in them similarities. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such where there is moisture as well as poultices; and there are some that are hard and stony in the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not go against it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are that you use to every instrument that is called "intromissioris," because its form comes after here, what it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, let him apply warmth from above to the long.  
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, then scrape without leaving the hair which contains that moisture, because it returns quickly when one leaves it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain after this are cleansed.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the wound; then cure the wound with ointment to that which is suitable, until it be healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, then cut according to this form, long; and place your probes there, and the skin on all sides, and put all your care into draining the sweat where it lies; and if the artery does contrary, then do that which I have told you after. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same with an abscess if it is purulent, and of the cutting and curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision upon the pus-filled abscess and the moisture is lighter because they are of little blood.  
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated or chiefs of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if one had made any incision on it, one would have done to him as well a wound as with a stone.  
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, for that which comes at the chief of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening shall be always at the lowest point, so that it may better discharge pus; and the cure as is fitting.  
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen at the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes come elsewhere on the body, and are bad, and lie one next to another.  
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous is properly inside its coat, like the nut and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofuls are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health.  
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that therefore which you see of good disposition at the touch, and seems to the color of the body, and mute from each side and is not harsh to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not deep; so it is necessary that you cut it from above, and the skin of each part, and keeping the two lips of the heart apart, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and the treat piece by piece, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and do not be the spatula big nor trenches, that the hands escape, and do not see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound powdered vitriol, or any powders that restrain blood, and constrain the wound; and leave it as long as the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to ripen. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then examine with your index finger if there remain any small pustules, and cut them and drain them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrofula a vein great, then it does not behoove that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it hang by it, without annoyance; then apply to the wound old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire scrofulous [boil], it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no delay of superfluity for the size of the scrofulous. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	So it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and drain pus, and treat it as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens more; and pierce as those before said, in depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is remained of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, there care of ointment to bring on flesh, until it be healed. 
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinance, it is necessary that the cut of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be opened; and one should not help them because all the veins and the prominences of the sick person are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the prominence, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four with a small slit across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable to the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from which. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the neck, then cleave the heart as far as it comes to the windpipe; and escape the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the windpipe which leaps from the place that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed of which one doubts strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the heart, and cut all alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, so long as it be healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim said that one should not do this until the throat is completely constricted, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the failure of the lung.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and she put it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the pharynx; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead.  
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and well that it had not been opened a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I made it haste, and thus I closed the wound, and I cared for it until it was healed; and there came to the lady nothing but that she was hoarse of voice, and returned afterwards to her disposition; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should have no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and is a large abscess in the color of a boil, and it is mostly in women; and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no engine.  
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat to us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work to do beyond this one that is small, and prove and search at all the intruder: if you find it as I our fat, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as we cut the ours, and treat it to its whole point, if there is any; and enclose well soon, and cure it as it behoves, until it is perfectly healed. 
des nous	of our (ones)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many manners of us there are, which I shall say all the resemblances; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference which is between our and exit.  
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an issue is sometimes feverish and hot, as long as the boiling has not passed, and is complete the rottenness; therefore, rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains the pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a bruise, and becomes big; and there are according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division.  
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of wounds, that you first examine and inquire about all the instruments that are called "entromissoire," according to what its form will come or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of probing abscesses as we do is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two pokes and pokes, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then when it is according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, and be careful in what jumps. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs short, what color it has, do as I said of other abscesses; and if after the introducer none comes moisture, know that it is fat, so treat it in a cross, and take it with pliers, and scrape lightly on each side and ward the cot where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the spout; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then drain it in pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Car if it stays there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve you, apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and constrict the wound, and put above soothing things, hot poultice, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the swelling is great, stitch the two lips of the wound, and cure from that which engenders flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beating is contrary to you or otherwise hurry and apply the place of powdered vitriol, and let it lie two days or three, as long as the wound rots, and rest the boiling of blood; then return to cover those that are remaining of the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments for pessaries, and they are in III ways: large, medium, and small; and there are III squares called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and there are in III ways: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistulas; and they are also like needles with which one sews sorcerers' spells, and they are of citrine brass, or iron, or silver, and most valued are those which are yellow, and are more proven of black plumb to enclose the curves of fistulas; and they are in III ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the probes are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are probes that have II curves of III manners also; and there are probes that have III curves, and are also of III manners; and there are probes that have II curves, and probes of a single curve only, and are of III manners; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these things is made to cut, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, because they remove the flesh. For this reason one does not harm the vein nor the nerve; and of these instruments are the alemeles put back in handles, so that the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses; and they are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses none more than on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places. And sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling a fist-shaped scalpel, according to this form, for which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed sometimes in the place where there should be a cutting of veins, and arteries, and sometimes reopened according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they seem like a woman’s breasts; and remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, he must follow this form according to these lines from b to g. 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if it seems to be cline down, and is softened for its size as it happens to women, so make it in two ribs above, by two similar incisions; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the loss of blood, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it moistens the remaining fat, then cure it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulous lumps or boils and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those then who contain moisture ought to be cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
