Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment beforehand as long as it is healing.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar appearance to scrofulous ulcers, then treat it as we have said in incisions of scrofulous ulcers, and if the wound is full of pus, then administer cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn above it, then many times abscesses come, and just as often it happens to the vein inflamed and abscessed; and if you know that this is because of the artery, so the abscess is long along it; and when you feel it at your fingertips, you feel a straining; and when it is because of the vein, it feels hard and swollen in appearance; and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even when it is below the armpits and under the arms and on the neck and in many other places, and is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron treatment, and in that which is at the head, it is also necessary to avoid, and in that which is of artery inflammation made from above the skin long; then work the waist as soon as possible, and depart beautifully the artery from the webs, until it is discovered; then put below it a needle, and make it pierce up to the other side, and strain the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place that is between the II ties of an intromissoire until the pus that is there comes out, and make the abscess open; then administer the cure that encloses the bow, until the tie holds; then cure those of ointment coming before these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, you must hold in your hand what you can from the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle below the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be the double thread, so that you pull it out on the other side; then tie the abscess as I have told you, or tie of one of the II parts of the II chies of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads do not come out, put another needle to all the thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and strain the threads in IIII lengths; then cut the abscess until the superfluities come out, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then put on top the draping wet with wine and oil, then administer cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are rubbed, or by too much labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often to shoulders and hips and in all their places where there are joints, and it is the grief of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in more dispositions without pain; and when one constrains it, then the patient feels pain, and is not completely formed of the body, but below the heart; and moves well from all sides, and does not go neither forward nor backward, neither down nor up, and the one that is in joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would go into contraction; and the one that is on the head or forehead, make the skin to the spatula. 
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a hook, and flay it, then empty it and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in the belly and nowhere else, and is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and the roots are fine, and the head is large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had II in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine root, and they were partly cut, and moist came out from them. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I weighed them and found in one XVIII ounces, and in the other VI З., and the work in incision is that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root; if the cope at the spatumile wide, and be in your presence the cautery at the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the hip often come many times very great hemorrhages of blood, and if the blood does not stop, then quickly you cauterize it; and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision of iron, then take a thread of lead well made, and in bind the limb as we have said, and let him for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to restrain the thread of lead until he has bound the limb, and cut by him without work; and if the roots are large, then fear to cut the same way for the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the skin which is of fox color and poor with pus and milk. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has broken open, and I will come to the treatment of sores after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has matured
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of a wound or fissure of the skin, and it is on the belly and has some of the boils, as they have in other ruptures, or of blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if this is from the rupture of the skin and the exit of the boil, then the color of the abscess seems like the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from diverse issues.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its sides, it rebounds, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it in your hand, do not constrain at all; and if it is for blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it feels soft to the touch, and the work is that you look if its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary that you leave the care.  
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have said to you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the boil, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be extended straight, then feel all around the boil; then command him to gently move between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess upwards to the entire great incision; then tie it around a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the two ends be loose; then operate on half of the abscess extended on the thread, and put your index finger, and feel the intestine; if you find it caught by the thread, then untie it, and put the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the boil, take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery makes it contrary, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II through threads, and put the II needles around what you have done in a cross that you make perceivable; then strain the abscess on IV lengths on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will dry out, and let the dead flesh fall away by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and dried up, then cure of what it should, and cover the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it should be, and weld the place.  
dou chancre	of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of ulcers, and how one must work on them with medicines, and how one must avoid iron cure; and let us say that an ulcer is avoided in moist places, and great caution should be taken in its cure, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be scraped like an ulcer that is in the armpit, and in the groin, and similar places, and it must be entirely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not fitting that you approach it, for I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the works, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge at any time the patient of black cole; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then make the patient i. good place to do the work; then set your incisions or sores, and the hair from all sides, and the bone from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow completely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the hemorrhage of blood makes you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is extinguished; then cure him with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; this is exposed only; and one must not touch iron in these two likenesses: namely, tympanites and hyposarca, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called “eclyses” with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as coughs and diarrhea and similar things; if one does not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness but dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part of the thigh, then take the spatula spine according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be deep cut of two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and nonetheless be not so deeply inserted that it can come to the intestine when you put it in, and cannot stitch it up; then look whether the dropsy is formed toward the intestines: if so, you should cut into it from below the third part of the blade III fingers directly above the hilt; and if the dropsy is for the disease of the liver, then make your cut on the left side of the third part of the blade; and if it is for the spleen, then on the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lies on the cut so that superfluities do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and bring it out, and raise your hand across the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as in scraping to the quantity of an ungle or more; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the level eight, and this is the place of the water, then pull the syringe, and put this instrument out for this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver knife, subtle, and it is of iron or lighter arch-metal, and on the lower part, I have a small hole; and on one side, III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the pen: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now on the instrument. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt on the patient, and give him much water, cure him with burial or hot sand, and with sweat or bath and in the sun, and let him drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At no time are born children who have no pores on the penis, or the pores are small, or they are not in their place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then immediately so he can perceive all of the spatula very subtle according to this form:  
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place or put in the fine clove of lead, and tie it and hold it so for III days or IIII and when he wants to urinate, have it removed, and let him urinate, and then replace it; and by chance it does not suit, because the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose piercing is small, so it is medicated with the lead of plant, as we have said, so it will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the part in their place are pale, because none are born with the part at the head of the penis, which is why they cannot urinate before they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and this is a bad illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies usually on his back, and are the head of the rod and the cope as well as the waist of a pen, so that the pierced falls in the middle, as it convieneth; and keep yourself from overflowing of blood that often comes, and if it happens, then the stanch of those who stanch blood, and cure the wound until it is sound.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils come in the rod, and it is an appearance of flesh ugly; and there are malignant and non-malignant; so it convieneth that you prick them with .i. oncine subtle, and the cope and cleans all, then put up cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is sound.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of bad color and pus, then it befits you to bring cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have grasped it, and if the bone is in some place of inside the skin and part within and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the bone which is inside first; and when it is joined, then care for the part outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, make sure the head of the rod is not pierced, and blackening and corruption come to its rod and where it joins; so cover all that is black and corrupt, then apply on top a poultice of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and veins, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two ways: that is to say, for the letting of blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must put or lead on the penis a chain of lead, and urinate the patient among; and when the skin is raw at the head of the penis who have not been circumcised, or they have for wound or for abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument's edge, until the connections are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a grievous thing to devise this, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any point of the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate between the two, and put the subtle linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not dry out. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound of continuity like the others; however, when we do this work by our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work, and the lightest to salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have nothing more than what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have wanted the most part of masters and healers who practiced circumcision around one dal, and with force, and at all times with a new scalpel; thus it was their custom because there are two cloths, and by chance if one cuts above and remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is necessary to cover, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is with the hole of the member it is not assured; and in the purification of the elbow by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they did not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is made with force to all the linen of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car when you press your hand, so it is equal in I whole soul tense; but that the child be well straited to the skin; and let the manner of the first work be as if you make the child think, if it understand, that you only tie the string around the rod just so, and then allow him to rejoice in all ways that you can; then make him stay between your hands straight, and put the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and blow or heart, and bring it up as long as the head of the rod is inside; then purify it well of the dirt which is assembled there, then tie the place signed with a double string, then tie it below I poc at the other lien; and hold it as II does by the second lieeure to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then lift the heart upwards gently and bring the head of the rod; then leave the blood to flow a little, because it is the movement; and put powder on and on the powder I drapeil glued with an egg yolk cooked untampered with rose water, confit with good and fresh rose oil, and let it stay until the next day, and cure him from another cure as long as he is healthy.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the purification is this: the two heads be held and be sharp, and be the heads also as large as the hand evenly;
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the leaves make an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce for three days, and what is below the shaft is swollen, let it be as long as the abscesses are calmed and the scabs are slightly scraped; if you can cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will not harm him at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, heal the place of things suddenly with a wound powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut out the kernel beyond measure, and it goes upwards, it will not harm; therefore cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from a stone, or blood congealed, or bowel, or fatty tissue, or similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is in the urethra or neck of the bladder, then it behooves the patient to be bent on his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above his back, and restrain the patient’s legs as much as he can; and thus it constrains the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it behooves you to administer an extraction with all the instrument which is called a “syringe,” from this is its form: and let it be made of fine silver, light-headed, like the feather of a bird; and let the shaft be a palm long and a half, and let it be thin at the head. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take I double thread, and tie it to the head I piece of wool or cotton, and put the head dou thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it until the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin d'uef, and make the patient sit on I seat, and raise his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tede water; then gently put the syringe in the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis upwards towards the bud; then put the syringe forward until the bladder, and feel the patient come until the void thing, and this is not done according to this order further than for those who lead or where it goes is twisted; then is the thread at all wool piece and piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine; and restart the syringe as long as the bladder is emptied, and be aligned the patient. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood comes in the bladder, or there is an assembly of rot, and you see it distilled with sharp and medicines, do as all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leus chevez by which the medicine short be such that it stops well the shaft without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see fit to put your medicines in the bladder, put the chief dou keusteur in the moisture, and train with the traiant that is within; so you will drain the moisture to the kesteur, and then push back firmly the traiant within; so the moistors will enter within, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster by which one clysters the bladder: it is here:  
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of bronze, and the head is higher; and below to the breast where the bond falls; then take a sheep bladder and put in the moisture that you see the clysterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good double thread, and heat the point of the clyster on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the anus, then strain your hand over the bladder to all the moisture coming down, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly throughout; then put the strong thread in these pierced holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dial, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.  
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have just said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder more often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water leaps from the bladder similar to water in its subtility; and it appears harsh, and grieves the patient his penis, and he can many times, and then it enroids; and with much of these leaps the foundations are made; and it is light the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as the middle to those who are between youth and old age; and it is the cure lighter of those who have the large stone, than of those who have it small.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it hinders sometimes to seek the stone. 
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and push them out and move down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it emerges from its high position; then make him sit between your hands with his arms under his thighs, so that the bladder is all inclined downwards; then grasp and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone.  
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch of all, so moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put it in its foundation, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, push it towards the neck of the bladder; then press upwards on your finger, and put it out to the far side where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him that he extends with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where the incision is made; then put the spatula cuttingly, from which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the hips and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight above the stone, and the two sides are either foundation or above, and let the waist be with a traverse so that it is wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps press the side which is foundation or above, so that it may go out without work; and know that there are such stones which have angles, and margins: if it is pierced to this; and if it is like one with a glint, and rounded, whose outlet is light. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To this one, then where there are angles and margins, make the incision greater; and if it does not come out, you should extract it with pliers which are like a file at the head, in order to strain the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you put under it the subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot manage it this way, then enlarge the hole of the passage, and if the stone is loose, then extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first put the biggest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the larger one comes out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more. 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very great, it should be treated, and make a larger wound. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Car two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through the place where the legs cannot close; but all the same, you try to treat it, or to break it with pliers, as long as you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, you put on the wound incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and you restrain it, and put on top of it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then bind the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, carefully moisten the area with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basilican ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and because of this urine is held back, which is known in such a manner that without leaping with the urine: therefore you must drain it in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and cause burning; then raise the wound with water and honey and seil, and help him in all the ways that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you care for him, that you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place.  
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the urethra conducts, and is tied within, and the urine cannot issue; so the cure of those that I say thus, that you cut it many times, and are excused from the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus. 
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron shaped like this and have it fitted with three points on one end.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the forest into the shaft lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand on the stone point by point, as long as you can feel the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone which is within the shaft. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken, and bursts with urine, and the patient heals; and if you cannot do this for any reason which hinders it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod straight against the stone between the two threads, then extract it, and untie the thread, and cleanse the clotted blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are present in women, and if it happens at any time, it is a serious ailment, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a woman well knowing who discovers herself to the eyes, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the woman's stone is more inward than the man's, so it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity arises for this, it is necessary that you take a wise midwife, and with pains, find one, and if you cannot find one, point does not desire I cast aside a subtle mirror; and present her a well-knowing girl in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her about the examination of the stone; and look carefully whether the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to thrust her loin or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she constricts it under her loin, and recommends that she thrust her loin or cone with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder form.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder down, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it is seen to appear, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its two above the stone or below, and let the tail be first small; then put the rail into the waist, if you feel the stone so across the wound as long as the stone can issue out, and know that many kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large and rough and soft, long and round, and which have reins. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances to know the outcome.  
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the sinew is weak, put on vitriol ground finely, and hold it for an hour until the sinew is stained; then return to your work, as long as the stone is present, and have instruments that I told you in the extraction of the stone to men so that you can help in your work; and if the sinew is weak, and it is the artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and strain with bandages, and do not begin again this, and leave the stone and do not draw it out, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the limbs are numb, then return to your work, as long as the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Watery ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the under part of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called 'syfac', and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these did not have this point.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the testicles, and is expanded that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either it is declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is re-open, I poc long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the skin itself, then the abscesses are re-opened with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white sac, then it is felt well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine the entire introducer, because its form is as described before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the repletion of his body; then lay him on his back, on a thing a little high, and put under him many cloths; then sit on his left, and command the minister that he sit on the right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the heart of the sides; then take the spatula clean, and cut the skin of the sides among them long until near the heel, and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the sides up to the white bone, and peel it subtly according to your power; then pierce the white bone full of water at the wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your bandages, and extend the white bone upward; and do not touch the heart of the sides, but only the white bone; cut everything or by pieces equally well, that if you do not cut it wisely, it will return the water; and if the union has failed in your work, put it back in its place when you have completed the work of the white bone; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the sides with one suture, then cure him as other wounds, until he is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the bone corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the bone along with the entire suspender, and draw out the bone, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; if you cut the other part as well as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put on the wound a pad half in rose oil; and put outside another pad half in wine and oil, and put it on top of the two pads, and put doubled cloths on top, and tie it up with all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and use wool felt according to this semblance and be assembled by stitching in the groin of the breeches, and one of the heads presses on the foundation up to the back, and the other to the armpit; and the other two chiefs above the two angles, and be all assembled the restraint in the loop of the brazier; and at any time is medicine this branch of cautery in place of iron size, and it is that you prick I cautery knife subtle, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syrup which contains the water is uncovered; take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syrup at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cope in all ways that you can, as long as you sear everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the eye; and know that this work is more safe; and moves guarding against loss of blood, and moves that the works of size; and if any thing makes you contrary, or abscess heals or loss of blood or other thing, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not wish to endure this work because of its horror, so administer a perforation as I tell you; and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that water root is there, then make the patient sit on the elevated seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below to all the width of the spatula, and put the perforation long through the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and leave for the remainder of the water to flow out, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to issue from the mouth of the wound, then you must pour into it a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of dropsy, for its form is before mentioned; and enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or whenever it comes around, and when it is assembled like before, and thus will pass the days of the patient.  
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch there is fear in more dispositions, for which it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and resemblances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the genitals; and it is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and aguish, which is spread to the joints, or by percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find any pain, and is a painful abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grieved fearful and stony, and of foxed color, and at times comes from none artery, or swelling of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is through an artery, so it is known by the arrangement of hot abscesses, when you press it with your thumbs; and it is not appropriate that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the vein's inflation is known by his disposition to the touch of the two, and one can well make the cut on this semblance, and on the other parts; and it is that you strike the core of the veins, then the egg is above, and the thread of the white side by side, and deliver the suspensory from all sides of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already joined with these new vessels, then it is necessary that you draw the yolk, and cut it; and if it is adhered to the sac, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all of that, and cut the roundness. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or its rear, it behoves you to cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the works are accomplished, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then the cure of other cures until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling the onion, with softening of the boils, and the patient moves painfully when it goes; and the cure of this disease is as frighteningly well as this one before, and nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then put the suspensory of the testicles down to your two hands, all the vessels which are near the member, and the masters tie them and stretch them; then cut with the sharp spade wide through the middle between the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then put a needle where there is double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle straight, according to the length of the body, and pull out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as with the others where one injures a bowe, so that no vessel should be cut which nourishes one of the testicles; because by this nothing comes to harm, and if to all the vessels comes blood, it is necessary to drain the testicles to all the vessels; so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment for the incision of the vessels, and dry out and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The happening of this ramification is by the section that comes or there it happens, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either at the syfac or of the extension of it, and these two manners of much come from causes: whether percussion, or leap, or braire, or lifting of a heavy load, and by similar things; and the signs when it's of the extension of the syfac, there are pock and pock, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal until the midpoint, because the syfac tightens the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the pus, that it brings a sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears various ways, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are drawn with the pus, and it is held in, and causes great pain to suffer for the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, because one should avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;
