et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to return the intestine into his hand into the wound, if it can enter; then be supported on his neck between your hands, and raise the hips; then hold the heart upwards, and cut all the skin of the groin along; then put inside the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and so that the bowels may issue; then scrape the soft tissue which is below the skin of the groin, until the white soft tissue is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into that which follows the groin, in that which is between the white soft tissue which is below the skin of the egg, and between the second soft tissue, and depart that which is behind the egg, and between the second soft tissue; and then move with the right hand into the heart of the groin, and hold the white soft tissue at the top to your left hand, and raise the egg on all the soft tissue towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the egg upwards, and untie that which is behind the ligament; and inquire with your fingers if there is no intestine enveloped or white soft tissue hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it into the back part of the soft tissue, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the chives that appear of the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the soft tissue, of which we have said that it is below the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then envelop the chives of the threads, and tie them formed of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except an abscess may come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread II fingers of it, and after these II threads leave the soft tissue which is below the heart of the groin the width of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the groin, as much as the sinew, and the bow, as we have said before; then administer wool soaked in oil, and put it into the wound, and put into it the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And at any time is cauterized the white fascia that we have said, after the incision, out of doubt of a flow of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens, and leave the thread as long as it hangs from it; and if it is slow to come out, so that it be risen with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it comes out; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch which is assembled with the vein, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and cure the abscess of him who works, until the vessels bleed; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the inguinal region, as we have said, and it opens the legs; and no parts of the bowels come out to the groin, and if any do come out, it is little, and repairs all hours; and anyway if it remains too long in this point, then the wound or abscess grows, as long as the bowel comes out; and this happens because of the extension of the abscess which is in the inguinal region, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and swollen the legs and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and that is that the patient lies softly on his back between your hands, then cut the skin of the rupture inflated by the width according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the abscess which is below the skin that the inside, then take the thread and put it over the place appearing of the abscess; and press it to the bottom of the belly, then stitch the two legs appearing of the abscess onto the top of the thread, and stitch one and the other; then extract the head of the thread, and do not cut the abscess nor extend the gut or anything else, as I have made you know in the cure of the ramification of the bowels; then cure by the cure of the wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse it and treat the wound, until it is healed.  
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The face is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the contents within are softened, and it becomes visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and he cuts the skin which is softened on the natural skin; then assembles the two lips with a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the sutures, and the cure as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of the  castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterization is practiced in our law, and for this reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the wise should be able to answer when asked, and know the cure; and the other, because we often have need of cauterization of some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and calves and other animals. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that cauterization is done in two ways: by attraction or by cutting. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and pliable; then taking them with your hand, until they are set and you no longer feel them.  
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of tail: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut above each testicle with a blow when you have well scraped them; and leave no prick or subtle prick which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is more effective than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing remains of the testicles, because the beast desires lust; then care for the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to II manners in men: the one if it is that between the II sexes opens as well as the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it comes about on the point as well as a rod and they copulate.  
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of man and woman is that you cauterize all joined wounds, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of their penis, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	Of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wart is a growth attached to the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tendon with your hand or awl, and trim it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest bleeding occur, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed; and for another sore that arises at the mouth of the furrow, and the ear, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the likeness of a cow, and because of this, the ancients called it "cow disease". 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary for you to cut it, as we have said the tendinitis, and care for it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural by birth, or by accident by disease that came to it; or it is by flesh joined, or by subtle or thick syrup, and is made through in the ribs, or costal, or below, or where it may be; and prevent conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these is by the regard of the belly. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is near appearance, if you want to at two or to the root.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If he is to be treated with subtle syfac, and he is near the two books, then hurry, and do this: put the two fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, legs spread; then extend the two books, so that the subtle syfac is round, and covers the swelling; then take wool, and wet it in oil, and put it over there, and let the woman lie at home each day, so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the abscess is hard and thick, then you must cut it with the spatula like a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stupor is of flesh origin, then suspend it to the hinge and cover it; and have the medicines that staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, together with a handful of egg white; then administer a bandage of wide linen, so that the wound may not close; and thus for length of time, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes new matter, it should be covered according to this manner, if it is not inflamed abscesses. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is festering which is in the marsh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without custom become accustomed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thick; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve healing.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the boil, when they are full in the marrow, and do not appear to the touch, except for the cure by iron.  
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, can feel, are those that can be cured. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the tumor with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding comes out, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confection it with honey and aisil, and with that make a plaster on her back.  
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he stays still, it is good.  
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it is not so, apply cupping to the back and breasts without injuring; then take linen, and moisten it in plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, so care its place of ointment until it is healed; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the harsh chief, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; and then the cure until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses of the flesh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the marshes, such as chancre and pus-filled abscess, and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It therefore befits me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not like abscesses that boil; and if you want to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is thick at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let him be made better until the pain is appeased; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have he small seats or he may lean, and support on his back and assemble his feet towards the outer part of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good linen band; then turn him to the right side, and there administer the instrument which is used to open the mouth of the belly, from which after comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see to administer this instrument, that you make the point first in order to know the depth of the belly, so that what enters into the instrument does not come more deeply than it should, and that it does not pierce the patient; and if the instrument is larger, then it is necessary to cover the depth of the belly with cloths, so that the instrument does not grieve him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument above, and that he hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and one softens it with their hand, then it is fitting to cover the head with a spatula, lead; and when the bowel is emptied, it is fitting that you put into the wound damp tents in rose oil or green dry oil; and place the tent from the wound to the edge of the margin, and put outside above the margin and on the linen cloth clean moistened in water or malves should be cooked; then cure after II days of ointment coming to this, until it is healed; and at no time lift the margin and the wound with a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lily and aristolochia long are cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is set back in its bed, it behooves you to guard against iron cautery, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	A profession is first to the delivery that she knows the figure of the natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down low, and desires to smell the air: then it hastens the child to come forth; therefore know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it is the issue under its head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is fitting to gently press her belly, so that the child comes forth soon; for when it descends upon its head, then the secondine is with him, and the mother is delivered of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes at times on its feet, and comes toward the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes on its belly, or spine, and is converted by chance on its neck, and other bad forms; so it is necessary for the healer that she be wise and subtle in these things, and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth loudly, and the virtue of it is weak, then have her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and rose her nature of oil or fennel seed shall be cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose form is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the secondine, and cut at its fingernail until the moisture that is within it is expelled; and hold the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with fennel seed mucilage with sesame oil; then make her take and sneeze from condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus now the child will be born. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands are out, it is necessary that you put them back gently one by one; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a seat, and raise her feet up; then overturn the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when it is overturned; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the neck which is in front of placed, and extract the child, and put them back evenly.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon his feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on his feet, it is necessary to push him upward; and then turn him back and forth, until he is equal; then grasp his feet and extend them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Let him jump to his hips, if he is commanded to do so, and have him cough from the condition; and jump further if God wills it. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, then turn it back and forth until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take musk from the high altar, and oil of sesame, and gum resin, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in a hot bath until under the ribs; and when she is softened there, make her colic with myrrh, and put it down below, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, because the child now leaps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, she puts her hands back and forth on his waist; then she is placed on her back, and she hangs her legs down, and lying on the bed; and she bends her hands back and forth, and then she takes her hands over her belly, and she removes the cushions underneath, until she is laid down; and if the child does not jump up, she takes his legs and moves them forward, then moves the belly upwards, then puts her hands in; and holds the child back and forth; and commands the woman to hold herself tight as long as the child is coming out.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of the child which comes out with a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It behooves to engage in bringing the hand back; if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then have her lie on her bed and straighten her legs; then administer the poultice that I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on the stool, then study in bringing the hand back; and bring the child according to its natural figure, and have her sneeze, and command her to bear down as long as the fetus is coming out.  
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child upon his neck, and has spread her hands, and her face turned towards the back of her mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient hold his hand, then turn it back and forth, and lightly; and when it is equal, he places on the muscle layer of height and oil, as we have said, then commands him to move it back and forth; and when you have done this, you make her sit on the seat, and command her to press; and she sneezes. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to the entire shoulder
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner to the whole secondine, so strike the secondine at your finger, until the moisture is emptied; and if the child cannot raise its head and neck, then cut the bud so that it is not retained, and kill the child; then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to refrain from any movement: therefore she will give birth easily. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live, if they can be named; I know those, that they should be multiplied, and are divided by the syfac which devises them, which is bound to the bud; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one all under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are coming out badly, the cure as we have said, and be the bail subtle, and quickly make and lightly what she does; and do so as it is worth moving to salvation.  
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, because by chance similar things happen; so do according to what is necessary. 
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her shoulders be inclined down, and the legs raised; and the minister the tail of II parts, where she is bound to the bed so that she is not moved by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the marrow with moist oils with mullein of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then oil the ball of her hands with these oils and these mulleins; then put them in the marrow lightly, then take where she puts the pins that should be suitable for them, and take ward if the infant is appeared that it descends on its head; so insert the pins in its eyes or in its neck or in its mouth or in its palate or under the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then put it or prickle and at the sides of the body; and it is necessary that he hold the pin with his right hand, and place the bend between his thumbs of the left hand, and puts it to all his hand lightly, and insert the pin in any of those places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place against the other one, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then move them equally in one direction and the other, so they may pass easily, and let the one be toothed to hold them tight, as is the form here: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains a part, one anoints the basin of some of his oils, and puts them in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remain, he puts this oncine or higher place, and does this until it all goes out entirely.  
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes forward from the other, and it cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you should wrap it in a cloth until it is whole; then cut in the joint of the foot or at the wrist, and so you should do with the other hand, and both feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or it has a sharp point assembled, then it is necessary that you put the pointed spatula between your two fingers, and make the head and extract the sharp point; or you can do it with the instrument called "almidach," so that its form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way, do if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull out the bones with forceps, and if the head goes out and it is strained by force, then split it, as long as the moisture which is or worse issue forth; and if it cannot issue forth, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is inflamed in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture runs out.  
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mouth of the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or the breast, then it is necessary that you take it out with the cloth wrapped on the hand; and make the belly or the breast, as long as the moisture there is gone; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then put the handle of your hand to enter into the marrow, and draw it until the mouth of the marrow; then put in the string or II, and pull out; and if the mouth of the marrow is constricted by a hot boil that has come, then it is not necessary to work, but it is necessary to administer moist and greasy things; and administer plasters, and siege in soft and moisturizing water.  
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it even, administer those that we have said in a living child; and if one has no power, so it will be treated by pieces, and leave nothing of the second skin. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you will have done this, if it happens to him those things which we have said on abscesses that come in the marsh; and if bleeding occurs, then be put in sharp restraining, and administer other treatments to him. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been stillborn, then conceived another upon that one, and refused the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time it came to her an abscess in the bosom, and it inflamed so much that it opened, and began to great pus flow.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I pondered long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and out came one bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because this one whose belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in my hand bones, until the woman was in better condition; and I saw the woman long time thus, and she did it back a little bit of good; and I have not recorded this chapter for that reason, because when the masters find a strange thing, they should know how to help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the bone to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the forceps, as it is written in the books; and to two turns as two handles of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle in the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft must be wide, and the edge of the trees it must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs should be adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are put in the mouth of the handle to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar in appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pliers; and it has two jaws adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and two wide; and when you see opening the vagina with the entire instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, feet hanging and legs open, then put the two jaws together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then operate your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the patient does what she wants.  
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the one sees them appear, so much is the work hastened, and higher to the men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument that you have not appeared it, because their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is held back during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to hold her arm, and then make her sneeze from condiments, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well is.  
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not done, then take a pot and make it perforated, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, whether cooked or steeped in water over the fire; then put a cord or perforated around the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and tie it until the vapors come from within the marsh; then make her sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If it jumps back suddenly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no force, command the woman to soak her left hand in oil of sesame or in the muslin of althea, and then put it into the vagina, and pull on the second one; and when she has found it, seize it and stretch it back and forth gently, so that the thread does not break during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes and breaks. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the nostrils is inflamed and squeezed shut, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, so guard that you do not use the milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the nostril, that you tie it to the hip of the woman, then the clisterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon; if she will bear and put back, and will come good; but all ways, when she bears it so there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and pales the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary then for fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have experienced the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one fumigates the woman at the time of childbirth and afterwards is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let the fumigations be above the coals, and the tinder as long as it is burned, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, but it is stopped with a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife that she pierce that syfac at its place, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatumile, and guard the lacement so that it does not touch; then put on a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not stop up, then put on a piece of lead upon the wound, and leave it for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stoppage comes from the closing of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that closure: if it is cured, as we have said about the cauterization of flesh.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from below the foundation are nodules, and larger ones that come from near the foundation of fur, or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and still moisture surrounds white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas disappear; and they are known by those who have them with discharge or flatulence when the patient defecates, and by chance some jump out. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if the fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and to half the penis; and reach up to the groin joint, and to under the hipbone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula piercing at the foundation, and not piercing; and it is that you put your left index or foundation, and put a subtle needle of steel or iron in the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has a twist, put a tent of fine lead or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair at your fingertip; and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission from the opening or wind nor pus, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so haste in curing. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or up to the urinary duct, so that urine leaks out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the thread comes to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around, then it is that it there is bowe, and there is no medicine nor cure by ointment; and in these fistulas passing there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of fools who meddle with them. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither too young nor too old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proved, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined to his belly; then put a tent of araine, or of plonc if there is curvature, until you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the base, then you should put your index finger there, so that when it tugs he feels it; and be discovered or you feel between your finger the syfac or the flesh, then know that it is pierced; if you do not work it at all one cannot cure it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says forthwith that one can well heal some, but this happens rarely; and the help one makes, if one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and put it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and do this II times or III, as long as you know that these charred fibers are burned, which are resembling a feather of eye; and then cure with moist tents in butter, as long as those chars isse were, then cure with ointment enjaring char and soldering.  
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, well.  
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is so, it cannot be cured otherwise; and if it extends in between and does not pierce to the root which is or foundation, and between your thigh and the tent you put a thick covering of flesh or silk, and you see the fistula at the end of the covering that follows the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the tent, and then apply the cautery afterward, as long as it comes to the head of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and fall; then remove those fatty tissues that seem like a feather of an owl, and there remains nothing. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the without-skin goes in, and is caught between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine sharp.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined bones and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then the cure of wet wounds in butter or crushed herbs, as long as the flesh lies low, and if the chars are burned in the cavity; then cure the wound with hard dough bandages, and they are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way down to the very base, and is separated from the body, then you put your finger or foundation in, and examine them.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or syfac or chars, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways except by the way of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the III manners: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure it as before; and don't allow them to be too deep in that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and let the evacuations come by the way of willing; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound once it is cut below the foundation, or by tent or by another appointed instrument; then cleanse the char faultree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: this will be lighter for the sick. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is or rests against the base of the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form: 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And one puts two threads twisted together, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pushed into the edge of the base within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you push your finger or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and restrain it no times, until the threads have joined those that are between the two, and stick; then cure the wound as long as it is healed and sound.  
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make for the lacing covering if it is too deep, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatheous spine from which one makes the fistula is very acute on one part and trenching; and on the other part no, for that's why one does not cut what one should not cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes are according to II manners: or they are inside the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short above blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the chief of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and still above or a little bit of citrine water or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the foundation, is that you command the patient to stretch himself to go into rooms, until the foundations leave him, and appear the sons; if you hurry, and you can hold it with tweezers, or you hold it with your finger, then you cut it at its roots; and if the one-sine cannot hold them for their moistures, so take them to the drapeil, or to cotton, or a piece of chamelot; and they are extracted to your thumbs, then you cut them, and powder above some hot powders that be in their place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery, since the cure of other cures until it is healed; and if the foundations cannot leave, so you clistrize the patient with a stinging and harsh clister to wash what is at the foundation, so that he can clearly leave; when the patient stretches, and if the sons are outside the foundation, then the cure is light; and is that you take them with your finger or tweezers, and you cut them, then cure them as we have said, until it is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron. 
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the suture in this manner: take one thread, and put it into a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be it of the wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do this for all the others, and leave one to drain the superfluity of blood; then place on the foundation a piece of cloth moistened in rose oil or in cerote, and put it on top of the foundation, and command the patient that he rest; and then let him rest until they are dry, and when they will be dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until he is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Through drying of the fevers or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying of fevers in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and the medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it get moist; then treat it as long as it heals as it should; and if it cannot heal, re-scrape more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	about trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants is a little appearance false before the body, and go much in through them; and sometimes it finds them cold, and feel him also like dead of trembling, and comes in all the body, and more to the hands than other part. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill of an owl's feather, or a vulture's feather strong, and put that quill on the wound, until the purple circles stain the wound all around; then turn your hand over the whole quill until you cover the whole wound all around, and put it in its proper place, and scrape the wound from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see this, do like that of a dog's iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not let it pierce, so as to hold at the two, and move pressing; And if you see this, cauterize the vein, as it is before or chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes a clyster is made of silver or copper, or melted iron or mesh; and sometimes these instruments are made small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those then whom one administers care to for children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large is above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is an opening where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and on one side there are II holes, and on the other I; and the belly where one puts medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there is I space; then put in these holes I strong thread of twisted silk X or wherever it encircles, and assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie the string in front with a strong thread, then administer an enema; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the clyster with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then put it in gently; then, sponge the ministers at his two hands together, until it is all visible, then withdraw the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to issue, let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps through the night entirely, then it is more help. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema for the sickness of a falling belly, and the medicine rushes out quickly, let it return as many times as necessary until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base, or an abscess, then use a clyster as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin should be strained: 
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by striking of stone and sword and knife, or by spear or club or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head simple, because remembrance will come in its chapter. 
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it is of a stone hit or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt an abscess: so make it bleed both from the cephalic same as if it comes little blood from the wound, and be the bleeding opposite to the part numb; and eschew the patient's repletion of wine and of thick meats.
