Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let him lessen his food and drink no wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in stippled wine; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved by the air, put on some ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then assemble them by stitching, as I shall say about wounds of the belly, of the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to bone, and hangs, and holds only by a piece, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat thick meats, like beef and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.  
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting skin and it does not reach the bone, so cut away all the rot, and throw away the pus, then cure; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without a doubt, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put into this powder which binds so that when the wound has been cleaned.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood II parts; quicklime III parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime when incense or dragon's blood are not available, but that the fire has cauterized the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has healed the wound, even in the state [of healing], do not put on this powder; but place some digested ointment, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it becomes soft; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with a wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pliers; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes to the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other means than to leave it to heal, and do not put anything restraining upon it, because it does harm to the nerve and makes it retract; and do not put upon the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as chalz washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucie washed also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it and bind it with bandages, then care for it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is capped and full of bow, then pierce or lower them; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes, then cauterize it, and loathe it, and cauterize where necessary is; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the conduit is kept, because the flesh goes, so sew the heart above the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it according to its natural figure; and then restrain it well, and leave it for a few days, then cure it with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then cover it; and if there are pieces of bone, treat them all so that you may, and those that you cannot have, let it rot until the wound is free and aligned the exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.  
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if it has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, see if from the wound there is an exit of wind as the patient breathes: then know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, do not put anything to it in the first hour, nor tie it up so that the blood does not remain in depth, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but I put attractive ointment, and I bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there comes no spasm, nor tremor of the heart, nor strangling of the breath; and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.  
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat therefore with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, and work, know then that there is a fistula; so treat the wound as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then the cure of those who are in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is deep in the bone, and has broken pieces, then close the wound, and treat the fragments if they are exposed; and if they are not exposed, then let the wound rot, so that it will lighten the extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs is the judgment as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound sometimes the intestine, or nerve of the intestines, comes out by which the introduction of others; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than the small wound the large, because for this reason one puts back the intestines in, if one does not put them in hot and cold; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they return in more painfully, and therefore it is worth a hundred pains the middle wound, so that one must reset the intestine to its place as the others II And know that the rupture of the belly is according IIII manners: the II sutures common happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and II other sutures proper are common to other wounds; and all the same they are more suitable with the suture of the belly, and I will say one each and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine has been thrust out, and it appears to be easy to put back, then it is done by one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water alone, or you cook in hot water with squill and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and at no time do this restraining it, and it is moved that awe only for to deflate. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and make sure it is cooked well, for by this they are aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument with which one operates on hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to moisten that tail, so that one should not cut it without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: dig inside into the curve and outward no, and see here the form:  
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails have burst out, you put it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you are able, because this is valuable. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part below the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your attention to that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large and medium wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	The small wounds put that which is appeared to you, then have between your hands I minister pitiful who holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of stitches, and is that you prick an awl or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound I measure of space, and there stick an awl where it has I good strong thread; and pierce the II heads of the skin with the II heads of the syphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the II heads of the syphac the II together; then the strain of a double thread around the awl of II parts, then assemble the II heads of the wound in agreement, and then leave I measure of space, and there stick another awl; then the tie of the thread as you have done the first awl, and do not cease of this doing according to what you have need of the awls, until all the wound is restrained; and let the awls be mean, between subtle and thick, for the subtle awls cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well enter: for this reason it is necessary that they be mean; and do not come to put the awls too far outside of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the awls, so that they do not bleed the patient while sleeping, and put tents or drapes at the heads of the awls for them to hold, and leave them until the wound is sutured; and this manner of stitching with awls is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices an awl or II in the second stitch. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back his intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I treated him, and he was well.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the seer had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one could not find any, nor any medicine; and I put some fine cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with water mixed with honey until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the heart in a straight line, lay the point on the place where you have stuck the needle, or sewed, and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitching is that you stitch as the furrier does the furs, and that you leave the thread one time on one side, and take it again on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suture, as the Galicians say well, is like any fountain that brings together the two parts naturally, and attaches one chief to the other, in this manner: pierce an awl or needle close to the point of the suture, and feel the hole alone, and leave the two ends of the suture; then turn the needle and pierce it from the outside part to the inside, through the two ends of the suture; then pierce both sides from the outside part to the inside, with two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common manner of suture. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the other parts of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh in all its blood, just as the fire has moved it, so put back the intestine, and the coat; then put on powder with a healing char, and if the fire has moved it, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and stitch the thread, and be soldered the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, put on, as soon as it begins to heal bowe, old cotton, and move it two times a day until it is healed. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten a linen cloth lightly in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and below the buttocks; and if it feels pain or rot in the bowels, which happens many times, then give enemas of black wine, and also if the rot comes to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the plantiness of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the rib jumps from the wound, put it back as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black, then you must tie the place that is black, that bleeding does not come there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and put the two heads hanging from the side below the wound up to outside in order to align the extraction when the rib falls, and the wound bows.  
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured, and the wound is small, it may be restored in some men, for I have seen that a man was wounded or belly of a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and was infected and became a fistula, and through it there was evacuation and flatulence; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until he was healed, and his bowels were joined.  
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the patient did not have pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and said certain experimentors that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take threads with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has covered the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that it strains its mouth upwards; and then cut the head, and it stays so that it cannot untie, then put another thread afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely surrounded; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is heated in the intestine, and there comes no harm to the patient, and one can tie the intestine of a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that it be well cleaned, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of fine linen twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it in the rupture; and this manner of stitching of intestines is not more than according to the way of marriage and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing but subtlety.  
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is healed and then bows inwards. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knotted false and white thing, where one feels no pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it appears clear, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times large; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only due to one of the IX causes: namely, by the small amount of blood or body; or for its evil; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the wound is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a type of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and slow healing, and inflamed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and signs, and cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I make you know the cure of fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so forth that comes to the property of the principal member, and to the similar ones. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to where I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it known, so take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, so the query; and if the fistula is crooked, so the search with a subtle tent of cork, because the cork bends easily around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well search it by tents, so clisterize it through one of the openings, because the moisture runs from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then query sagely in your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is chased deep into its way, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, so cope according to what I have told you, and remove the false parts and the corrupt matter that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep and straight place, so it is necessary that you cope deep into its way, as much as you can, then put moist tents in a medicine of water, and put them to the head of the fistula, as long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is laid at the bottom; and then put ointments of healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cope. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve does not harm or main limbs as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat the king as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure things with bandages until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns as before, know that you are not yet well done: if uncover and go as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore its place; and if it is thus healed, it is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not so, know that the corruption is too far gone, that you cannot fix it; if there is nothing else to do but let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and do not leave even one; and if the moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, cut through the moisture and flesh, and free the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place upon the wound something preventing decay, and let it remain until the flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, leave only so much corruption until the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part corrupted, and comes right up to the marrow of the bone; it must be sored and covered all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is joined; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example from it and help in your work.  
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was one young man around XXX years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the materials came to the leg and he became swollen with a large abscess and there was no outward cause to open it; but the doctors through their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they corrupted much of the matter, and it became a fistula, and there came much pus that all lay bowed and moist from the body; and many doctors treated him for around II years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed through the fistulas to great extent; and the young man's skin became red, and he had a yellow color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I probed a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore began, and scraped in one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I saw what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not heal; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and considered myself able to close the place; but I could not do so until I scraped around a palm of the bone, and the piece was full of its entire width, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and healed quickly, and no longer needed to be reopened except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood often, but he was healed entirely, and there was born in place of the bone a hard cartilage, and he was of good disposition and had no nuisance nor contrary in all things, neither to go nor to come. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it should be treated this way: take a thread, and strain it to the head of the bone that opens, and command someone that he extend it upward; and put another thread of wool thicker than the first thread, and tie it above the flesh that is below the bone, and stretch the head, so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and uncover the flesh in the place where you see it should be, that the skin does not bleed the flesh; and put a splint or a board under the bone to move the corrupted flesh; and it must be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and be treated another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the entire flesh; then put the stick below, and then tie it from one part to the other the corruption, and be the linen thread long as the corruption itself, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and tie the bone where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is nothing else than to cut; and if the corruption is in the thumb of the hand, or in the thumb of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it opens for you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not oppose you; and know that the instrument and the threads to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their thinness, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip each kind of work its tool; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so consider the instrument which you need according to what is fitting. 
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder can be affected by internal or external causes; and when you have medicines for that corrosion by the cure of the medicines, and they do not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes by this from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it had been burned by fire, and after the blackness, then goes that corrosion of limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; so hurry to cover it, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the top of the arm, cover it, and do not give him any space to come up to the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and all thus do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes in the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes on a foot, cut the whole foot; and if it mounts to the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way but to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or cauterizing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend some ministers one of the ligaments down, and others ministers the other ligament up, and you sever the flesh which is between the two ligaments at a spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize, and put on each side a cloth of linen, so that the cautery does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess.  
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place carefully, or put some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb wrapped in a strong bandage, and cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and that corrosion first came into his big toe of his foot, until it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and a long time later the corrosion returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that were repulsive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he begged me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of repelling the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, that he would die, because the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have told this tale only for this reason, so that one may do otherwise, if one needs it. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place and stays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus; then it bursts and breaks through, and the pus pours out, just like blood vessels; and the skin which is above is as thin as delicate silk, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called “sain,” and is not called “fistula”; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone, then it is called “fistula”; and the skin is that you cut all around that skin, and even when it is thin, as delicate as silk; and does not hurt because of its corruption.  
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not yet in full force, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat with a clyster as follows: see if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, then give a clyster of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take asafoetida, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put them into a vessel over the fire, until the medicine becomes red and as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and restrain the anus; and leave the medicine inside for II hours, then remove it by straining; do this many times, until the breast is purified, and the bad smell is removed; and once the clyster of water from ashes is used, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them, then filter it, and clysterize with it, as long as you know that the breast is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine or the water from ashes, then clysterize with water and honey, where there is a pinch of pounded litharge; or clysterize with honey and sweet wine, because honey has the property of purifying and washing, and wine makes the flesh airy; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well purified, then clysterize with that which produces flesh in it, and it is that you take diaphinit plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or clysterize with some medicines and ointments, of which I have said the properties or treated of ointments; and if the hole in the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter it, then enlarge it with an iron a little, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, as long as it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up leaving only the place where the clyster can enter, and if the hole that gives off foul odor is above, then put the plug or lower down the part where it is.  
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in place, let no flesh get in the way; and if you cannot cover the breast as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner that the bow goes to the lowest point that it is, for when the bow is in place, let no flesh get in the way; and if you cannot cover the breast as you see fit, arrange it in such a manner that the bow goes gently downwards, and let nothing of the bow remain; and take medicines that consolidate to put on the wound, and stay upon the linen sheet that covers the whole wound; then cut as forces at the opening of the breast, a little wider than before; then place ointment under the other cloth according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound to align the bow, and do not remove the large sheet for many days once; and the one who is on the opening of the breast, often removed to remove the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in such a manner, and you see the nature that jumps on the wound, know that the breasts are already closed, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest lies bowed indigested after many days, know that the chest does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, so do not despair of health, for health approaches. 
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite; and if it hurts to be a chest after many days, know that the breasts do not heal well; and if the breasts take long to heal and are swollen, then apply medicines drying moist ones in substance and dry ones in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, because there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and the same is done better cooked honey, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them on honey when it is over the fire; and then glue it I drape, and put it over the breast, and sometimes administer one long aristolochia, and roots of celestial lilies, which are also like flour of roses and wormwood; and use of simples or composites: grind them, and make them into powder, and put them on the honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is too deep, and has made an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on limbs; so the cure of the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaritium is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand, or of the foot, or perhaps in other places; and when it becomes inflamed, and one does not take care of it, then comes a purulent abscess, which spreads and spoils until it reaches the root of the fingernail, and perhaps all of it; and the corruption comes up to the bone, so that there is foul-smelling pain, and the limb is very swollen, and its color is inflamed.  
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut at it with iron all the superfluity that is remaining from the joint, then cauterize the wound afterwards.  
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and begins to prick, and bleed, then it is necessary that you put the root under the nail so that the flesh does not, and push it upward, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then you cut it and treat it well, because as much as the bone is corrupted, so it cannot heal; and if you see that it is about to corrupt, you cut it at an angle like it was said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and pushed, and the patient feels great pain, then you must first heal it. Then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on it which soothes.  
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the hand's soreness
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is a part where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us of the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any kind of [joint] of the knee does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the knee, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such manner: cut it at its root with a broad spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint, he is grievous to cure; so you hold him to be covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or must at the end have a nout, it behooves you to first cut the flesh round about until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable shape for that, then cure it until it is sound. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes to the two joints together comes from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from the burn of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut that suture so that the parts rejoin according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not join together; or you put between two pieces of fine wood, until the ends are joined, as it is fitting. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If soldering comes to none of its two with the palm, then cover that solder as it is fitting.
des vils	of villages  
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels wrapped full of melancholic superfluities, that come in many parts of the body; and more often happen in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than in others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once purging with syrup, and then the healthy of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein, and draw it entirely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The tail is done in this manner: first arise the leg with hot water very strong, until the large vein be softened, then restrain the leg of the patient from above the hip to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in I place, or II place, or III place, with a wide cut, then lift and draw forth the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the patient can endure; and then tie it, and command him to stay with meat eating dark soup; and recommence the evacuation and the bleeding when the veins are full, and hurt the patient.  
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The elevation of the leg is done in this manner: place the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, then heat it by fire, and then cut the vein from above the knee to the foot, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with an incision, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when it is felt; and it can be seen red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; then put the point beneath, until it is lifted from the skin, and then place it on the incision lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the point, as you have done, and place it on another incision, as you did first; then cut another section, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cut it at the heel, then raise and lift it until the second section; then extract from section to section, until it is all pulled out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull it up and lift it, then put a needle in the very strong double thread, and tie and lift it, and put it beneath the point, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and there is harm to the patient; and when you have treated it entirely, place a wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound; and cure it until it is healed.  
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the sinew is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it in a twisting manner, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to strike the vein is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is of a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is the shape: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in land that has no moisture; and it may happen elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of rotting that comes under the skin, like it comes from inside the body, snakes and worms, lodged between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that in the leg there comes a very great inflammation, then it changes its color and the vein begins to burst forth, as the root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood from one and a half to two fingers, and tie it, and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it has any point to the fire, then wrap around the wood, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and wrap the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it is all out; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring abscesses and rot there, and bad illness; because for that thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the top, and leave nothing in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of the palms of long, or ten, and one time came to me, who had it from ten palms long, and when you cut it, it throws out the root, and pierces it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and be emptied the matter that is inside, and administer medicines at the place preventing rot any day, then cure it like abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein hands fail, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot or foot, and there comes much bleeding, and from which it leaps blood; treat then as we have said before. 
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms which are born between skin and flesh
