Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This sickness is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens many times to oxen, and it is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the alert of limb to limb, as long as they touch the skin where it goes, and leaps further; and it is engendered by rot of some humors, such as come worms and serpents and lumbris and ascarides in the belly; and doubt one of its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him cured and treated, it is only possible to do so when he goes: therefore, it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong linen tightly, then cut above and treat the furuncle, and if the pus comes out from deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dries; and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the eye, then restrain below him the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and treat the furuncle; and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of the body of medicines solutives for the humors carried out, and avoid eating meat that causes rot. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen those whom I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a little after, I saw it rise as a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything else, as lively silver when it departs from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then a little after it corroded throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she felt it return around her body, as I saw.  
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed greatly how she moved so from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have wanted many that well had want to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and exposed veins, and because of that appeared that constricted windiness; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this malady, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, so lie above and below gently, and then cut above until that constraint of windiness is out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, so cure him who displaces the windiness, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.  
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large points, and small, and haired, and joined; and those which have II angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one which falls in any member falls according to II manners: or in principal member falls, such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestine, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls therefore in any place of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears to you: then it is necessary that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound.  
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the saliva is flung which is on the brain, is when there is a scotoma and a sudden and inversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of mucus; and perhaps without saliva from the nostrils, or from the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice; and flung out of the wound moisture white seeming to pulses, and flung also like burnt flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then keep away from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were fixed in a hard thing, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves like the hand, and brings dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: so know without doubt that death will come. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move its root is that without pains of foam leaping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great pain and sighing; and moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps it jumps from the wound any thing from the indigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and it jumps a point of fiber through the intestinal road, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and back spine and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are saved according to various provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do it in the same way.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the man with an arrow that lodged in the root of his eye: I examined it, and pulled it out from another side under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without feeling. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And they treated one game with an arrow that fell into the fat of the eye below the paper below, and the arrow was replaced, and they could only reach the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was big as a Turkish bow, with all its iron light without ears; the game was healthy, and he did not have any bad accidents.  
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treated an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully until I removed it, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treat an arrow to a man, that it was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then when he had passed XXX days, it did not change its disposition; I cut on the arrow, and  engulfed it, and treated the wound, and there was no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen or into his back, and the wound was sewn shut; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural positions, nor finds annoyance in any of its natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, who had an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things.  
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow to the prince's man, who was in mid-way between his bones, and was a little leaning on the right side; and the arrow was completely withdrawn I was called to the care after that it had been fallen three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.  
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with a very subtle touch, and did not feel it at all; and he sensed prickling and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the splint on his hand for several days and closed the wound directly, and he kept it there for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his knee; and he told me this. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound corrosive medicine for several days, until it was open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened in its place; then I adjusted it in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly; and it remained well for four months, and then expanded so much that the wound that I put inside the pliers, and the mine on one side and the other, and could not issue; therefore I did not cease to subtly invent instruments, until I took one day the pliers well made, according to those whose form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treated it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I therefore restored it, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was healed entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on those things which I do not say, for the books cannot fully comprehend; but the wise masters compare to a very small thing, and on those which are present and lacking, find new works, and new instruments, at the descending of strange things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not in the limbs where they are fixed other than according to II manners: or by their place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is said to be through the place where it enters, it is an arrow entering into the flesh, and it is never seen again. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it as long as the cartilage is swollen and inflamed; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and it cannot come out, leave it so for some days, and move it every day; and then it will jump, and if it does not jump, pierce around with a fine probe until the area around it is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not draw it out, but leave it until it is healed after several days, for if the arrow comes to the syvac, it is death.  
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come to the surface and remains with the patient for some days without bad accident, if the engine of the milk. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply lodged and cannot be drawn out freely, then administer poultices as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and it cannot be seen, so search the entire wound; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you can not because of the depth of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, so cut until the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if there are ears to which it holds in the wound, then remove the flesh that is stuck on both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as much as you can to draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, that you may pull it out more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then lay it until the place around it is softened, then treat it, because extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes it contrary, administer what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and guard against incisions to the nerve and the vein, and put anything how you can move the arrow without danger, whether soon or late, or firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do it, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees or feels nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in that place: cut therefore upwards, as much as the pliers can take hold, and then extract it: if it has leaped now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, leave it still and then begin the extraction again until it is drawn out; and if it were of the arrow, thrust it all the shaft; and if the shaft falls, and you see to administer a binding, then administer the instrument headfirst, so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrow is lodged, put the instrument headfirst again, in order to facilitate the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then cure the wound as it should be done.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or in the belly or at the bladder or at the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it up, if you cover it; and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if it is necessary; and cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat arrows are similar to the beak of an eye, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the cutting point is like that of an owl's feather, to pierce at the tip of the arrow, so as it is shaped: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the pliers for putting and holding is this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one gets well, of this it has or head XVI, that is to say: II batans that are after the ears, that are called the two «herbech»; and the II arteries that are in II temples appearing; and II veins that are in II tear ducts of the II eyes, that are called «aspires»; and the vein that is between the forehead; and the vein that is at the chief dou neis; and the II guindeges that are on the neck; and the II veins that are in lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called «augeherich»; and II veins that are under the tongue.  
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly drained in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one that is drained, which opens manifestly over the pouch.  
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the sap vein is the one that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two veins there; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one of them is below the bend of the pocket on the left side; and the second, which is called "sophene," is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "ness," which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrh and migraine; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a bandage, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their places depending on the head: where then, to your right, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, so seize it; then take the lancet, and put it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to all of the vein above, and cut and the skin and the vein well two fingers thick through, and make blood flow out as much as you see; then tighten and bandage, until it is cured; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for ancient migraine, and sudden, and accustomed ophthalmia, and to the body of tears sharp as the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding is as I say: and is that the patient restrains his neck, so long as the two veins appear openly; and feels the pulse below your right; and then signs enche; then lifts the heart above the vein on your right index, and puts the lancet under, and raises the vein upward, and the cut, as you have done in other veins, and do cure of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right on the vein an hour, then put cotton; and then the lie form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cutting and their extraction, as the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein in the forehead is as good as the bloodletting from the cephalic vein for diseases of the face, ancient headaches, and migraines, and for rubor; and its qualities are that the patient strains their neck by twisting it until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "furrow maker", whose form is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the tip upon the vein, and press with your hand, or another thing, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein as long as it is healed and never work one of a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper that the flames are too large; and to heal across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts so aids the eyes, and to the ear, and to the nose, and to the corner of the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient strains his neck by twisting with any linen as before; then the vein, and let it be the vein through, a point through the long through the flame a point wide, because there is no flesh.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, perhaps it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein of the nose is good for fever, and for sores, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and boils that come in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient constricts his neck, then strains his nose to your left hand, and takes a fine subtle long thread, and puts it in the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin now to flow; and do not let it flow too deeply, and make flow blood according to your need, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the thread: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the II veins helps in the strengthening of the joints, and at the beginning of mesentery, and to many diseases, and to empties, and to corrodents, and to herpes, and estiomenes; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient strains his neck below one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the sick man, and the sick man lying on the seat, then vein the long one a little widely, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then redo another part in the other vein, then untie the linen, and restrain both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until the morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	Of the vein of the livers 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the lips above helps to heal in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and splits of lips, and sores and ulcers.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them because they are black, and because around them there are small black veins: cut therefore both, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and just as with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue so helps after the bloodletting of the cephalic, and it is at the stricture of the throat, and to the diseases of the eye, and to the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bloodletting is that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: so let blood from both, and do not let it go too deep, because below are the arteries. 
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut by which one commonly heals are healed according to II manners: or they prick at all I flame mirtin wide, or with a subtle olive like sharp trenchers, and it is called «anesil»; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and the fineness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very renowned, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins for blood flow of large apparent blood, and which contain large and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame: 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly; and it befits the surgeon that he bleeds wisely, and that he turns away from the artery which is underneath. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the ground and bleeding comes running, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said; and it must not be piercing flame, but cutting like a knife. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you must strain it, and change another; or you want any vein of it, or you open in its place the vein in the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cut to the flame anesil, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is fitting that you extract the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with chalk, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flamed vessel; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: avoid therefore. 
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude upwards like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and subtle, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten yourself then, and put your hand lengthwise on top, then remove your hand if the skin is tight, which often happens; if the arm is loose, leave it so, and do not move the patient; and be fearful, and do not move him until he is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it does not come out easily, and it pains you, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and bind the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of fig, and make it, and take one half and tie it well until the other day; if it without stinging, it is good; if no, cure it, as we have said, with powders that sting blood; and the stingers are not grieved in more dispositions for the small place of the wound, and the power of the ligature of the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm in the middle helps that she treats blood from the head above and from the body below, for this reason it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the healer to lay himself upon the nerve which is below, and if it is not too much pierced, and he finds the nerve, and he inflates and the saints are gripped, and by chance it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men for its subtlety, then it behooves you to vein it with the instrument anesil; and feel the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bloodletting of the cephalic vein helps, that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is fitting to bleed them pricked at the olive flame or the myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it does not have nerves nor arteries. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and it does not matter if one fails the first time, and one begins again; and by chance, the joint swells in some people, when one fails the first time, but it does not matter.  
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is administered only to preserve health and to avoid diseases to come; and be the bloodletting made in one of the three veins that are or cuta: namely cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one must bloodlett in the beginning of priens a geun, and in autompne and in yver after meal, when the sign of repletion appear; and one must bloodlett the first day or the third, after II hours or III dou jor. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting that is administered to diseases has no determined hour, but when it is needed, in all hours and at all times; and it does not befit to bleed children until fourteen years, nor a woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not blood let the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to bleed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary for them to cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if they have many phlegms held back, so that the veins do not attract superfluities from the intestines that are harmful to the principal members; nor should those who are too full of meats bleed, nor those who are drunk, as long as they are intoxicated, nor those who are dropsy-stricken; and it is worse to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiplication of labor for women, and childbirth, and wakefulness, and fasting, and any that are all virtues, or by means of the weapon or of the body; then purify the humors if they are thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then go into a bath, if nothing forbids you, in order to purify the blood, and bleed from the vein on the side of the thigh, as we have said; and guard yourself on that day from labor, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be light and joyful, and let the person bleeding be higher than the one who is bleeding them, and rub the arm twice or three times, then tighten the ligature above the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot properly control the blood; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell up, and you can feel them; then moisten the person bleeding’s skin with a little drop of old oil, then put his finger from his left hand on that vein below the point where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not escape or fail when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are like cords in the body, and some that are filled with windiness, so that when one puts a flame on them, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if it opens the vein, it is the wound too tight, for this reason it is necessary that the veiners be advised in these things.  
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, begin again a little below where it was cut or above, if it is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the lump is swollen, and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and not bind the arm: perchance an abscess will come; nor enter into a bath, then begin again the bleeding if he pleases; and if the wound is small, or the vein short subtly and you doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, then fire in that same opening straight throughout; and work a bit carefully, thus that the lump be swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the wound inflamed, do not begin the bloodletting again, and put a little bit of oil cloth on it, because it closes the body of the blood and is more moist in this place than the oil; and thus administer the oil cloth in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and these same things are applied as a treatment and poultice for them, when it is put on the wound; so subtly the pain goes away and it separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there come some abscesses large, which happen many times, even when it is not drained except at the time where the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and in wine a bit hot, and hold it an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days no blackening or greenish color, it does not harm him; and if you see, put on any thing of aloes or myrrh brought back to juice of calamintha, monarda, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances to the saint's basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft at the pressure of the hand, so is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore shun that you put on any of those things that we have said, for by adventure it comes short of the artery; but make i. plaster dry to harden the place, then cure it with other cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it ooze until it becomes red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it is thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is fat and full, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him often and little, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and nerve damage, and is more useful than bleeding from a long or a wide vein.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is feverish, treat him with blood III times or IV. And if he is of a cold constitution, moisten before the bleeding moistened bread in mucilage syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it pains at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of meat, and subtle fragrant syrup, and use the other things which we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of vein.  
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to drain his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body that is already exhausted, and it brings fever; so it behooves to draw a great quantity, and widen the opening as long as it flows in pameson; then when you reward all the conditions of health, and place your hand upon his wrist when he is healthy, so that death does not come in the place of pameson, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it does not behoove when you see to untie his arm, and make blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; nor if it is crooked, that he extends his arm greatly, for this would be bad; but let him leave it until he heals the second time; or you do not point to the flame, as long as the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein flows out, and put on top of the small amount of pus put back in place, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein of the arm is bled at the place of the vein of the neck because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of this vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well; then the incision is made now across, neither wide nor long; and let the punctures be wide, and let the incision be made well near the joint of the hand, and if he cannot withdraw it, put his hand back in hot water, and leave the blood to run until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not return his hand to hot water, because it is put in more in winter than in summer; and this vein's incision is safer of all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it works: restrain the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen, if one sees it; and if the vein is crooked, and if you cut it completely through, it does not cause any harm; and do not go too deep into its depth, for the nerves are under all naked of flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and wool on the wound to soothe it, and do likewise for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood of him in the left hand is worth to the sickness of the mouse, and do all as I have said to you toward right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bloodletting of the spine is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the legs, and retention of flowers, and diseases of the hips, and thighs and old leg ailments, and similar diseases. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his healing are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it purges, and ties above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot go many veins; heal therefore the one more wide, or at the ankle, than it is worth. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you vein it on the foot, guard yourself from the nerves that are below, and cut through it as well as when cutting; and let the flame be annealed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot pull out [the vein] from it, put the foot in the water and leave the vein well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the first incision needs to be made, begin the second one above a little, because the tissue is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the opposite foot equally. 
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the heel of the foot, and its incision relieves the pain in the hip when it is warm blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of its vein are that the patient enters the bath, and is strained above the ankle four times by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, then you cleanse it in all the ways that you can, and across; and it is better to move than to cut it, because the skin is dry, and it is very readily pulled apart by hand. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy any vein of him who opens or back of the foot, and toward the small thigh, and ward off the nerves; and make so much correction of blood that you see, and then untie the bond, and put cotton and restrain; she is now healed.  
des sainies de ventouse	of the wind suction 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or glass, or wood; and cupping is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done with fire, it is according to two manners: or it is with all fire, or without fire; and cupping that is done by striking and by the extraction of blood, it is done in fourteen places of the body, so one is entirely in the head; and the other is in the neck; and two others in the two ribs of the neck; and the cup on under the chin; and the cup on the two shoulders; and the cup on the hips; and the cups between the two arms; and the cups on the two legs; and the cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, but only of small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it weakens no one, as much as is done from a vein; and it should not be administered, whether with all fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to nosebleed, or by custom, we should introduce each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; for there are such that, when they have need to bleed, they have a heavy head; and there are those who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes; and those who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who dream, and see by nut blood and corpses and death and similar things. 
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is removed in the month, we command to ventilate after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the vein helps with the heaviness of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not suitable that this be done after the evacuation of the whole body; and this ventosation is in place of the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is not suitable for those who are of cold complexion or have phlegm, because it causes them great discomfort; and therefore, it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor those who have a cold disease in their head. 
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower because of the fear of obliviousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The inflation of the neck is in place of the vein of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is useful for the treatment of pleurisy, and for opening the channel of the diaphragm, and all wounds, and for repletion; and one should not blow too hard, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obstruction or in the stomach or heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, and headache and migraine, and to strangulation, and to the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the vein of the basilica; and it is necessary that you command the healthy one that he expresses his hand to put, that he does not cut the artery, and does not come running of blood. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation below the chin is good for mouth sickness, and gum disease, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations of the arms are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because they draw blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to prick them too deeply, because the skin is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries below. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The sucking cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below, and it should be big, and of iron, that it needs to well draw; and perhaps, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The sucking cups of the legs are used openly, because they draw blood from all parts of the body, and are good for old pains of the hips, and of the knees, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and they are placed in the place of two shins, and of two ankles, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in more dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the sucking cup is that you put it first empty, and successively, and place it gently, and move it equally, and do not cease to do so, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the redness of the blood; then close it, and replace the cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, because there are some who have fleshy flesh, and clear pores: therefore it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a deep hole; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, then it is necessary to strike .ii. times: the first time to subtlety the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, then it is necessary to strike the third time; and when we want to drain blood little by little, then we pierce only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want much blood, we often return to it; and if the vein is thick, so make a good incision, and the end that the hairs are punctured firmly, and it is necessary for one who has thick skin and hard, and who have many pores, you oil their cupping cups with perfumed and dissolving oil: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond sweet oil, or seed oil of pumpkin; and if it is winter, of cresson oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar. 
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, then take wormwood oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if to him whom one heals has tender skin and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil, but it is necessary to wash after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.  
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, rise from ash, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.
