And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or from their own water, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar; and it does not behoove to suck before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or II; and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is required that he be warmed, when he must be cupped and when he is cupped. 
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard yourself if the one who is healed is choleric, and if their body is too hot and inflamed; so it is necessary that they eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces at the meal, and similar things; and boiled beans, and veal broth, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and mince pepper, and mint leaves, and small onions, and pigeons; and on the day that he will be bled, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men once triacle or musk before bleeding, or afterwards, to comfort the principal members; and it should be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot should drink it.  
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied without hurting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the chest and the hips and the groin, because these members do not suffer to be hurt on their own, and one does it only in order to attract blood from limb to limb, such as we put on the breasts when the child is born; in order to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, such as we put suction cups on the belly and on the chest in order to reduce the limb; and remove the pain, when there is an inflammation or a stone, so it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the inflammation, or removes the stone from its place; and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, such as in diseases of the pleurae, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water which has boiled herbs suitable for this. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the leech administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it II has two of large and half a palm from top to bottom, and it has or costal around the middle I small hole, as if to insert a needle, and be d’arain, souef before so that she does not bluece the patient when putting on the limb; and it has in the middle a rod across of iron or of iron, to put a candle enclosed, and be them large and small according to the maladies and the age of those who take them; for the suckers of the children are other than old people, and the thin ones that of fat.  
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus put this suction cup onto the limb: take the candle of wax or the linen cloth and place it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and its sides should be over the opening that we have said, so that when one wants, vapor goes into it, and one removes the suction cup; and take the linen cloth as before, and begin again often, if you need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass which is administered in diseases of pleurisy, on any sharp pain, it has no handle nor pointed end, and it is not administered except when it is full of blood, and it is placed upon the member so only; and this is its form. 
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leechings are not applied except in members where one cannot place leeches because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar; and in the denuded flesh, such as two or three, and other similar parts; and the qualities of its use is that when you find leeches that are in clear sweet water without putting them on, take them; and put them in a nut in sweet water, until they are famished, and have nothing in their bellies; then be healthy with a vein and a suction cup, then rub the member so that it is red, and put the leeches on top; and when they will be full and swell, if it is the place where one can put a suction cup, put it there, because it is worth a lot after. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, lift the place with ease, then water, very well, and then tighten; and if the wounds heal too late after the body of the sinews, so soak the cloth of linen in cold water, and put it on top, until the sinew is stretched; and if the sinew is multiplied, so put on crushed vitriol, or gallstones, and similar things, as long as it is stretched; or you put on the place half of peeled beans, and let them there until they dry on the place, it will now stop; and if you need more of this, then take other sinews. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sutures do not want to be taken, so rub the place of fresh blood, or you put an awl there until the suture is pushed out, and then put them up, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will become firm; and when you see that they are falling, powder on a little bit of aloe and silk ground, or ash, so they will hold now. 
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear reader, that the fool looks at this chapter and sees nothing like any old books, nor has he read any letter; and for this reason, knowledge is absent in our land, because I have never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in these two chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if any thing does not help him, as weakness of body, or child, or old; or if his limbs are not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold things, namely cold drinks, and meat of lamb and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, as long as you have doubt of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; so the patient returns to his first governance that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourish the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or there is viscosity, as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of beef, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment it recovers muscles and more quickly the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit do not heal well or weld according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those who are too tender, like the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone with the large tendons which are near and join the limb together, as much as it was before; and for that reason, you must nourish them with thick meats, as we have said. 
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go inward, and others outward, like the point of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture with wound, and fracture at all a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner has its engine, and its instrument proper in the restoration, according to what remembrance comes to its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which the bone is twisted, and appears well by outside, and hurts at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no torsion nor hurt at the touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture; but it can well have torsion, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not need to move it with your hand, but put on the medicine that comes after, and then gently restrain it.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that goes in a bow, and are the II parts disjointed, it is now necessary to put them in equal points, so that abscesses come from there; and if abscesses come there, let him leave them for no day, until the abscess is appeased; then put it equal to the movements that you can easily and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of the one which has pieces; then restraint, as it is necessary after.  
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken in pieces, whether it be of the two parts, if it be hands or feet, or to the hand if it be a small limb, or to two cords, or to one cord and to the hand; and put the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken limb are separated, you move by all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two joints of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well by hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if the draw well and do not restrain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work abscess hot and contraction in the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor when turning, nor in any other manner; and guard well that the limb be so secure that it feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except a little point, and it is necessary to put it in such a disposition that he does not feel any pain; and keep him that he be placed straight, so that tortuosity comes not when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.  
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Car there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides equally, so that there is no gap; then bind around light splints, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and strain your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go to above the fracture and strain less, that the fracture then moves away a little the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you feel most of the healthy part, then take another bandage, and turn around directly above the broken part; then return to the lower part of the fracture, and strain it moderately, neither too hard nor too softly, as we have said in the first place above; then put between the bandages splints of linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or swelling. 
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on it a soothing postil of pus, and that removes the swelling, and let it stay like that for several days; then place above your bandages, and be half the width of a cane's length well stitched, or from wood from which they make clubs, or from palm rain, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts on the fracture be a bit larger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is necessary for the limb of smallness or largeness; then constrain on the splints as you have done at the first hour, then tie above with a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; more strict it is above, less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want works from the fools who make their ties with cords of twisted linen, and this is a great error, because the tie cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it does not become that there be between each splint less than two fingers' width.  
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is annoyed by the stings of the stitches after the tightening in their healthy parts, then put under them pads of linen, or felt wool, so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put splints for after 5 days or 7, or more according to your certainty of abscesses appearing; and see here the manner of the ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: and that you take flour that is held at the walls of the mill, and confit it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, not too bright nor too thick, and use it, and that is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in many dispositions, and even to women and to small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.  
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three parts each of honey, lard, and elecampane root, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mastic, ana .x. З.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. З.; and make it into powder, and mix them with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones well, and is worth much to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plasters that is good for torsions: take mugwort and wormwood, ana X III; myrrh and aloes, ana IX III; acacia VI III; Armenian bole X III, and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of  plastering to joints and bones dislocated from their places, and soothes the pain occurring, and the use for fractures: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and boiled in water, and put it on the place. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [it], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removing pain properly. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make a poultice that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground elder leaves, and grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of emplastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remaining pain of an abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marsh mallow, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of verbena, one part each; and grind, and boil with wine, and if the limb is frostbitten, boil it with moist coriander water, or water, and use. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another manner of splinting more firm than the first, when an abscess hardened comes to the restoration of the limb. 
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mallow, and seeds of flax,  mallow, melilot, and henbane, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Galen says in his book that on the broken member for restoration one should put a certain one made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two not too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken limb, to restore, things dry a little hot, as myrtle and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make a plaster that is good for the lesion and pain: take mugwort and henbane of men chopped, or feathers of owl, and viper's grass, and equal parts, and grind them, and make a plaster with it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then you untie it a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if the bones have moved from their place; if not, do not untie it for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the bandage now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of moist sea, and dip it in water, and raise the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, half soaked in water or in rose oil, and tie on a nut, until you are sure that there is a hot abscess; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin again the subtle bandage, and a little bit of bandage, and do not restrain it as strongly as before; and bind it subtly until it is healed.  
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and the pain and swelling are all gone, and you need plaster and bandaging, then begin again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb of those that we have said, then do not untie it except after III days or IIII or V or VII; and no time leave it XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and approaches the alignment of the bone together; afterwards restrain it more than before, and thicken its flesh, as I said before; and if you see it drying more than necessary, know that nourishments cannot come there; arose then with warm water, all times when you untie it, and let it be each third day, and moisten a bit the joint; by this work then shortens the nourishment in the limb, and mends quickly what foolish men do, who keep the limb twisted: this is bad, and so is the work dangerous, and I do not see anything else than to leave it and work directly. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by percussion of sword, and the collarbone all the bone until syfac which is below the bone, as made haiche or fust; and for this reason this way of fracture is called «haichure». 
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an impact embedded, or splitting or of the neck of bone, or of the thigh on bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture passing, which approaches to the membrane which is under the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound which is rejoined in the bone as subtle as a hair, and is the fissure small, and for this is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound that is made either by striking of stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes enter the piece of the bone down, and is the lews heated like do the blacksmith when they fire on the cauldrons; so enters the piece within.  
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or whose bones are moist, such as a child's; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are separated from them like stars; and I will speak of them in their place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by the traction on them, and the investigation at their ends, and by the corrupted cartilage that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of capillary blood vessels is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs on it, the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, be wary of accidents in the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of phlegm, and loss of consciousness, and swelling, and numbness, and fever ague, and the eyes are watery and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, then commence the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it behooves to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth under the bone may not be corrupted, and the accident that we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part as follows: and it is that you prick the head of the sick person deeply, and uncover over the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more carefully than you can, and if blood flow comes when uncovering the bone, or abscess apply, if he needs help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with bandages moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess applied is appeased, and be assured of blood flow; then begin to remove around the bone, and it is done according to II ways of work: one way is that you cut in a narrow strip in front, and this is the form: 
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of incisions of various types, some narrow and others wide, pointed, and made of iron; and in working lightly, that you do not crush the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must pierce it around it, so that you administer splints with chisels, not too deep so they do not pierce beyond the bone of the test, and it should have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have several more, so that each one comes in its place of the breadth of the bone, so that you may have chisels for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one chisel on the bone, and turn to your two hands as much as you know that the bone is pierced; then put the chisel elsewhere a bit later, and so do all around, then cut with the chisels the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pliers, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the marrow nor the syfac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have pierced the bone, and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the instrument which is lodged in the bone to all other instruments similar to a scalpel, but it is necessary that it be more tender and more subtle than the other scalpel; and if there remains anything of the small bones, or no scales, then carefully remove them with the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said. 
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; and he praises it very much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lens-shaped incisor, for that is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut in one direction and is the bone ague in two coasts, so that the trenching is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently break the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below; if it is attached to the bone, then gently remove the bone, because one removes it well without pain, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to carefully remove those asperities, and remove the scales with a fine razor which you must have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you start with large razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and subtle bone fractures, it is necessary that you administer care according to its direction; and this is something that is not fully repaid to one who has placed their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the ulcer is uncovered, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, that you do not hurt the ulcer, then administer by above another linen, and do not constrain it more than so much that it only holds the wound; and let it stay like this for a day or two, until the abscess is calmed, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of violets, and incense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer other medicines without mordant; and watch that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor let it come together bowe, because when bowe comes together on the webbed membrane, it will corrode and fester, and bring great harm to the patient; for when one puts on the ulcer a mordant thing, it will blister by above. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take guard then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the black spot does not come out except through the medicine that has been put on it, which has virtue, then it is necessary for you to take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil and in glue I drapel, and put it on the sore; then cure it in ways of cures as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts of the nose are never broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break unless it is forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you put your small finger or through the two, and put each fracture inside your index finger, and to the pouch outwards, until the two return according to their natural figure; and do this lightly, and guard that the patient does not feel pain by your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the knee and cannot come to its place, then it befits you to put it equal at the head of a stick one piece thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another band, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or the tenth, when the abscess has calmed, then bind to the chief with two tents of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind one on the other side, if the fracture is there; and let the lengths be so thick that they fill the hollows of the knee.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said any restorer one must soak the tents in butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the preparation of auburn of egg, and powder of mill; then leave the tent, as long as the bones are firm, and the cartilages hardened. 
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts down goose feathers in place of tents, and so to 1 souef drape it around, and hold the scalpel and blow on the patient among; or do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you are working on it, put cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in 1 pock of diachylon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour, and incense powder, confited with egg yolk, then put light pads on top, and do not tie it nor the bandages; and if the break of bones is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then you will extract it with suitable instruments to that end, then sew the fracture, and the cure of things injanrans char, and suturing, as plasters and ointments suitable to that; and if inside there is no wound, then cure it with bandages, and put inside bundles of wool, until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken from below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only superficial, and is not broken in two, except for a slight inward bend, if one knows it gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your left index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, you put your right index finger, and push the fracture inward gently, and hold it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is separated into two parts, it is necessary that you administer extension to the two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth happens, or rupture, so restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on the broken jaw cerote, and put on 1 double cloth; and put on the cloth a great star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it on as much as you can, and command the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so untie it on the third day, and then re-stitch what has changed; and put a plaster on top, of powdered flour with an abundance of egg or sesame meal, after which you have removed the cerote; and put on top a light cloth, and if the plasters harden, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a boil comes, so administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward so that no piece of the bone is removed; if subtle to remove it with instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, then sew the wound, if it is wide, and put on one layer of plasters suitable for this, to prevent flesh from growing, until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, toward the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners: or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is so when the fracture is without wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the broken forcele; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put each of the fracture to your hands, so that the form be as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor disfigurement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, so put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth, or wool, and be large according to your necessity; and hold and gently raise the forcele, and strain the sphere in your hand, so that you put each of the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder by force because it comes back in place, then it is necessary for the patient to lie supine on his back and put under the shoulder one-half hour, and push the minister's shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find it broken, then it is necessary that you cut above; and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join for any mounting, then cut with one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to ward off the shaft:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not at all curved, and be also wide as it needs, according to the size of the bone and the force of the work; and have II heads, as you see, and one be wide, and the others narrow, as is the fracture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so close the wound, and if the fracture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, so cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the abscess is hot there comes, so moist it. one drape in rose oil and in ash and in wine, and put on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incisions, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of yolk of egg, and put light bandages on top, and put a spear under the saddle, if you have need; then take a very broad band of a palm wide, then put the doubled drape above the bandages, and the plaster; then take a small strip of three inches wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the head of the bandage hangs down; and put the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage on the neck, and under the healthy saddle, and under the diseased saddle; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then reward it each day, and when the ligaments slacken, then restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put him when he sleeps a small pillow under the saddle, to raise the shoulder up; so will lighten the fracture of the arm by the raising of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and do not untie it until bad accidents come, until XX days; then renew the plaster, if you see that he needs it, and restrain and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most at XXVIII days, and in less for some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes it happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates in the middle, and only through touching is it known; so arrange the device according to the figure of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put above a double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is even at any point of the shoulder, use that hair from lin bandages, so that the splint sits evenly; and then restrain it to a whole great bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the ligament every day; and whenever it softens, bind it, and put back the splint if it is out of place, and lie the patient on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25, And when this number is completed, untie it, and be sure, because it is not a bone that easily moves. 
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes before and not under the heart, so do it above, and the bone, and make those things that we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the abscess hot.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens little; but it often breaks at the end.  
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in a limb, it declines to the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and swelling, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the passages in the broken bone, and it feels well. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and one puts 1 cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulders, and he brings together the sides of the 2 bones with his hands, and subtly does put it in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then puts bandages and poultices above the thin skin of salt, or some other light cloth, and wraps it in 1 cloth, and ties it over the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turns the tie around on the back, and tightens it well, and rewinds each hour the bandage, and if it softens, he tightens it; and if it is necessary to untie it, for corrosion or for itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and unties it, and cleans what has come up in ways of cures; then puts back the bandage, and tightens it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs comes only in their thick parts after the back, and at the top inside, and they bend only because they are brittle; and one feels it well to the touch on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you put the fracture even, as it is right.  
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then place the plaster, and restrain it with a splint, if you need one.  
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of ribs is sloping inwards, the patient feels very great pain and numbness, as well as shortness of breath, because the bone pierces the lung; and besides aches, and coughs and vomits a lot of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients put a great deal of care into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are some who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to drive the pleurisy outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for boils if they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say none of us put suction cups on the place, in order to suck out strongly, and that seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup does not draw out superfluities to the place for the sake of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one must cover the place with a woolen cloth in hot oil, and put a tent between the ribs to make it even on both sides, then be cured of the cure of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that pierces the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath an instrument to ward off the syfac; and then one must saw through the bone, and gently draw it out, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with ointments, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on it soft cloths in rose oil, and put them on top; and treat while the place of the abscess is covered, and lie down so that he rests on his side where it should be, as long as it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes a fracture occurs to the bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that they bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, if you take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it.  
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many positions, and if they move and feel good when pulled and held, know that the articulation of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured if care is put into it.  
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, then take heed if the legs are softened, and if the accident is that which is in hands, and on the back there is windiness and ejection without will; and when it is supported on its belly, there is ejection without will.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and it wants to sit down, it cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if you do not labor in its cure.  
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward if there is an abscess hot, then put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk of one egg, as long as it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and tie it with a linen band, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cover the joint with wool; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then cure with ointment that promotes flesh, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "head of the cow," put your fist of your left hand, and place it equal to the other hand on your power, then put the plaster and bandage on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are bones dislocated, do so again, remove the bone, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Few things happen that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, then there would not have been a little bit of lessening to the top; and making long, and declining to the sides, and comes to the patient pain at the place, and prickling, and swells what breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over, as long as you are over the fracture; and know what are the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is at the top only, then put equal that fracture, as long as it is to a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, then make gesture the patient on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture is apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it equal, place it on the plaster, then place a splint of wood or of heart, and restrain the bandage so that it does not move; and employ the place under the ribs, until the ligament is equalized.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient that he sleep on his healthy rib, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come to them, do not touch them, until the abscess has been appeased, and place on it what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and restrain it as is proper, if there are no bad accidents; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder fracture
