And when it is even, place a drying plaster with an abundance of egg white upon it, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of three fingers long, that  covers the site of the gibbosity and the side of the healthy spine, then bind it with a linen bandage, as we have said, and use the patient to a subtle nourishment, until he is healed; and if anything comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have mentioned before; and sometimes one administers a piece of plank, and sometimes it appears in the back bone of the spine, and one thinks that it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, so for this reason one must not have presumption: by chance would come death.   
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only with dislocations, and not like the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and poc dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the diseased knee than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend his knee at all; and is the leus which is below swollen with a hot abscess because the head of the hip comes there.   
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to fever, so this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in front, so are they well his leg according to accomplishment; nevertheless, do not double knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he goes, he passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind, so he cannot spread his knee, nor double, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and is the hip joint at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this appearance of dislocation is that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no cure; and it is not convenient that he has presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocations, so you haste that you return the joint, and the extension within and without, and the movement to right and left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you appear as minister strong, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or to the linen that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upwards in such a manner that he pushes his hands downwards under his armpits, then tightens a linen band on the hip; and another holds the head of the leg; and extend up and down all at once, so that the patient be lifted from the ground at one time, and remains hanging. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not done, it is necessary to pay attention to its appearance When the dislocation is at the shoulder, it is necessary that you support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen on the root of the hip, and the place which is below the groin, then raise the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the strength; then take other ministers to his arms, and embrace the large place of the hip which is diseased, and extend it outwards in this way: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this way that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the sick person together with a strong linen rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let it be suspended by the head on a pole, and be two arms' length above the ground; then command the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers hold the patient, who embrace firmly the hip, because the joint now returns easily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the back, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has stiffness, and restrain the limb on the bad leg properly, and on the hip too; then put two sticks, one at the top and one at the foot, then stick one stick between the thighs of the patient in the form; and lay a plant of damp cloths around, that it will not chill the bad limb, then extend each minister towards him, and the mire puts equal to his hand the dislocation.  
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, that is, and press it as we have said in the book of surgery, and let the patient lie on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put his pain on the front of the diseased limb, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the hip, it is not necessary to stretch the patient down, nor raise him up on the ground, but it is necessary that he be as if his hip were dislocated outward, as we have said concerning childbirth on the two hips; and let him be on his face, and the strap extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint to the table; and will be straight when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal; therefore adjust the hips, and put the splint, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest III days or IV, then untie it, and put the splint on; and if you see that they are equal, strain it, as before, and leave it III days; then untie it, and allow him to walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not rest at his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as far as he can, and put your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your two, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it rests lightly at his hip; and put the plaster on, and make the leg rest at the hip, and tie them together firmly for three days or four, then untie; and do not let the patient work, as long as the limb is fortified. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is sometimes bruised, and sometimes dislocated completely, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated: the resetting is light, and one must extend it lightly with his hands when it is felt only.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, it is necessary that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him by the legs, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left twice, then upward, and put the foot well up; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, lay the patient on his back on the ground, and insert a stick firmly into the ground between his hips, and tie bandages around him so that he does not bleed; then hold the patient's hip with one minister, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or to the ligature, so that they tie it above the ankle of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the stick should be well between the hips of the patient to hold him when we are stretching him; then put the fingers of each minister on the dislocation with their hands, and other ministers hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return readily. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set in place, put the plaster and dressing over it, and strain it firmly, and tie its foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the ankle behind, that the ligature be not too tight; then let him stay for II days or III, and if the ligature softens, tighten it; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for IIII days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to him, then it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and this is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or of the foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his flat place or on a table straight, and put your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it comes back; and when it is equalized, and there is nothing open, then put under the sole of the foot a board at the head, then strain it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is desired to restore it, many times the patient dies; so be not presumptuous in its cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor bold; and use at the beginning of things soothing poultices, hot ones, and let the patient be in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the boil may come to it again; and when the limb is in its place, administer soothing poultices, hot ones, and cure the wound as it is necessary, with dried dressings; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, set them, and do what has been said for simple ailments; and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and of your body. 
Amen	Amen
